###begin article-title 0
###xml 54 70 54 70 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 95 97 91 93 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 54 70 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
Transcription Analysis of Central Metabolism Genes in Escherichia coli. Possible Roles of sigma38 in Their Expression, as a Response to Carbon Limitation
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
###xml 43 46 <span type="species:ncbi:11866?0.5863095238095238|species:ncbi:12321?0.21726190476190477">AMV</span>
###xml 84 87 <span type="species:ncbi:11866?0.5863095238095238|species:ncbi:12321?0.21726190476190477">AMV</span>
###xml 121 124 <span type="species:ncbi:11866?0.5863095238095238|species:ncbi:12321?0.21726190476190477">AMV</span>
###xml 212 215 <span type="species:ncbi:11866?0.5863095238095238|species:ncbi:12321?0.21726190476190477">AMV</span>

###end p 1
###begin p 2
###xml 85 101 85 101 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 253 257 253 257 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 262 265 262 265 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 433 437 433 437 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 477 479 473 475 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 548 550 540 542 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 718 722 710 714 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 722 723 714 715 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 788 790 776 778 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 800 802 784 786 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 860 864 844 848 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 869 872 853 856 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 893 894 877 878 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 913 917 897 901 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 917 918 901 902 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1113 1114 1097 1098 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1109 1114 1093 1098 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1219 1221 1199 1201 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1551 1559 1531 1539 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In vitro</italic>
###xml 1711 1715 1691 1695 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1715 1716 1695 1696 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1795 1797 1771 1773 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1807 1809 1779 1781 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 85 101 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
The phosphoenolpyruvate: carbohydrate transferase system (PTS) transports glucose in Escherichia coli. Previous work demonstrated that strains lacking PTS, such as PB11, grow slow on glucose. PB11 has a reduced expression of glycolytic, and upregulates poxB and acs genes as compared to the parental strain JM101, when growing on glucose. The products of the latter genes are involved in the production of AcetylCoA. Inactivation of rpoS that codes for the RNA polymerase sigma38 subunit, reduces further (50%) growth of PB11, indicating that sigma38 plays a central role in the expression of central metabolism genes in slowly growing cells. In fact, transcription levels of glycolytic genes is reduced in strain PB11rpoS- as compared to PB11. In this report we studied the role of sigma70 and sigma38 in the expression of the complete glycolytic pathway and poxB and acs genes in certain PTS- strains and their rpoS- derivatives. We determined the transcription start sites (TSSs) and the corresponding promoters, in strains JM101, PB11, its derivative PB12 that recovered its growth capacity, and in their rpoS- derivatives, by 5'RACE and pyrosequencing. In all these genes the presence of sequences resembling sigma38 recognition sites allowed the proposition that they could be transcribed by both sigma factors, from overlapping putative promoters that initiate transcription at the same site. Fourteen new TSSs were identified in seventeen genes. Besides, more than 30 putative promoters were proposed and we confirmed ten previously reported. In vitro transcription experiments support the functionality of putative dual promoters. Alternatives that could also explain lower transcription levels of the rpoS- derivatives are discussed. We propose that the presence if real, of both sigma70 and sigma38 dependent promoters in all glycolytic genes and operons could allow a differential transcription of these central metabolism genes by both sigma subunits as an adaptation response to carbon limitation.
###end p 2
###begin title 3
Introduction
###end title 3
###begin p 4
###xml 139 155 139 155 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 472 473 472 473 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>

###xml 632 635 632 635 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores1">[3]</xref>
###xml 650 657 650 657 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 813 815 809 811 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 845 848 841 844 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">crr</italic>
###xml 876 879 872 875 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Glc</sup>
###xml 910 914 906 910 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 955 958 951 954 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Glc</sup>
###xml 996 998 988 990 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1041 1044 1033 1036 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Ueguchi1">[4]</xref>
###xml 1085 1087 1073 1075 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1159 1162 1147 1150 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Weber1">[5]</xref>
###xml 1164 1167 1152 1155 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Typas1">[6]</xref>
###xml 1264 1265 1252 1253 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1427 1429 1411 1413 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1429 1432 1413 1416 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores1">[3]</xref>
###xml 1434 1437 1418 1421 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Weber1">[5]</xref>
###xml 1438 1442 1422 1426 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores2">[11]</xref>
###xml 1481 1483 1461 1463 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1591 1598 1571 1578 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1690 1693 1670 1673 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Weber1">[5]</xref>
###xml 1695 1698 1675 1678 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Ferenci1">[7]</xref>
###xml 1700 1704 1680 1684 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores2">[11]</xref>
###xml 1705 1709 1685 1689 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Ferenci2">[15]</xref>
###xml 139 155 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
###xml 650 657 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1591 1598 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The phospohoenolpyruvate: carbohydrate transferase system (PTS), in conjunction with Crp and Cra, constitute the main regulatory system in Escherichia coli involved in catabolite carbon repression that allows the utilization of glucose as the preferred carbon source. This system, composed of several proteins, is the major consumer of phosphoenolpyruvate (PEP) for the coupled translocation and phosphorylation of glucose into glucose-6P. Strains lacking this system (PTS-) have a significantly reduced transport rate of glucose and other sugars, resulting in permanent slow growth on glucose when it is the only carbon source [1]-[3]. In wild type E. coli strains the presence of PTS makes it difficult to unveil the role of other mechanisms and modulators involved in carbon scavenging responses, such as sigma38. In fact, in strains lacking crr that codes for the PTS EIIAGlc component, translation of the rpoS messenger is no longer repressed by EIIAGlc, thus allowing higher levels of sigma38, even during the exponential growth phase [4]. This sigma factor takes over from sigma70 in the expression of many genes during entry into the stationary phase [5], [6]. In a similar way when wild type cells are grown with glucose as a limiting nutrient, and in PTS- strains that grow slowly on glucose, transcription of several central metabolism and especially glycolytic genes, turns out to be also under the control of sigma38[3], [5]-[11]. Thus, it has been proposed that sigma38 should be considered a second vegetative sigma factor because hundreds of genes are under its control when E. coli cells are exposed to stress conditions, including starvation and growing slowly on glucose [5], [7], [11]-[15]. Therefore, these set of genes could have promoters for both sigma factors.
###end p 4

###xml 139 146 139 146 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>

###xml 308 312 300 304 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Artsimovitch1">[20]</xref>
###xml 449 452 441 444 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Typas1">[6]</xref>
###xml 459 461 447 449 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>

###xml 544 546 524 526 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>

###xml 607 609 583 585 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>

###xml 703 706 679 682 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Weber1">[5]</xref>
###xml 935 937 907 909 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1132 1135 1104 1107 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Weber1">[5]</xref>
###xml 1137 1140 1109 1112 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Typas1">[6]</xref>
###xml 1142 1146 1114 1118 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Becker1">[21]</xref>
###xml 1147 1151 1119 1123 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Nystrm1">[23]</xref>
###xml 1297 1300 1269 1272 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Typas1">[6]</xref>
###xml 1302 1306 1274 1278 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Grainger1">[24]</xref>
###xml 1403 1405 1371 1373 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 1417 1424 1385 1392 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1522 1524 1486 1488 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1726 1729 1690 1693 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Typas1">[6]</xref>
###xml 1731 1735 1695 1699 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Nonaka1">[25]</xref>
###xml 1736 1740 1700 1704 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Wade1">[27]</xref>
###xml 139 146 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1417 1424 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Differential DNA recognition specificities of the various sigma subunits allows promoter selectivity to the RNA polymerase core (RNAp). In E. coli, the alarmone ppGpp modulates the binding affinity of different sigma subunits to the RNAp; high ppGpp concentrations favors binding of sigma38 over sigma70[16]-[20]. In addition, there are other factors such as DksA and Crl that apparently modulate the binding of different sigma subunits to the RNAp [6]. sigma70 and sigma38 are very similar proteins; in fact, genes whose transcription is sigma70-dependent in vivo can often be transcribed in vitro by sigma38 and vice versa. The current view about the "selectivity paradox", as mentioned by Weber et al[5], is that these two sigma factors recognize very similar promoters, and that minor differences at the -10 region shift the specificity towards one or the other RNAp holoenzyme. Moreover, transcription initiation by the RNAp sigma38 holoenzyme is apparently less affected by deviations from the promoter consensus (e.g. degeneration of the -35 sequence), which allows this holoenzyme to transcribe from "non-optimal" promoters [5], [6], [21]-[23]. In addition, transacting transcriptional regulators, such as Fis, H-NS and IHF, as well as DNA topology, can contribute to promoter selectivity [6], [24]. Remarkably and in support of the results of this contribution, the recent analysis of the sigma32 regulon in E. coli revealed an extensive overlap between targets of this alternative sigma factor and those of sigma70. Some degree of promoter degeneration apparently allows both RNAp holoenzymes to use overlapping promoters that share transcriptional start sites (TSSs), giving plasticity to the transcription process [6], [25]-[27].
###end p 5

###xml 1013 1017 1013 1017 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 1171 1172 1170 1171 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>

###xml 1327 1331 1326 1330 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores5">[30]</xref>
###xml 1365 1369 1364 1368 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1396 1398 1391 1393 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1422 1430 1417 1425 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 1433 1436 1428 1431 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores1">[3]</xref>
###xml 1438 1442 1433 1437 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores4">[29]</xref>
###xml 1444 1448 1439 1443 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores5">[30]</xref>
###xml 1627 1631 1622 1626 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spoT</italic>
###xml 1633 1636 1628 1631 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gpp</italic>
###xml 1638 1641 1633 1636 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndk</italic>
###xml 1646 1649 1641 1644 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ppa</italic>
###xml 1734 1738 1729 1733 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1809 1811 1800 1802 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1881 1888 1872 1879 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1895 1899 1886 1890 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores2">[11]</xref>
###xml 49 56 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1881 1888 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
We have been involved in the characterization of E. coli strains lacking PTS (PTS-), such as strain PB11 and its derivative strain PB12, which was selected for growth rate recovery in a chemostat with glucose fed at progressively faster rates. As expected, carbon flux analyses showed that PB11 has a reduced glycolytic capacity. Interestingly, the adaptive evolution process that gave rise to PB12 rendered an increase in its glycolytic capacity [28], [29]. In agreement with these results, transcriptome studies have shown that several glycolytic genes are downregulated in PB11; in contrast, they are upregulated in PB12, as compared to the parental wild type strain JM101. In these PTS- strains that grow slowly on glucose, poxB and acs are significantly upregulated [3]. Therefore, it has been proposed that in strains lacking PTS, PoxB (pyruvate oxidase) and Acs (acetylcoenzyme synthase) play an important role in the transformation of pyruvate into acetylcoenzyme (AcCoA). In support of this proposition, poxB inactivation not only decreased 50% the specific growth rate (mu) of PB11 but carbon fluxes for the conversion of pyruvate into AcCoA were doubled in PTS- strains as compared to the wild type parental strain JM101 and the expression of some glycolytic genes was downregulated in PB11poxB- as compared to PB11 [30]. Interestingly, in these strains rpoS, the gene coding for sigma38, was also upregulated (figure 1), [3], [29], [30] and its inactivation which reduces the transcription of all glycolytic genes, produced also a dramatic negative effect on the growth rate of PB11. In addition, the expression of spoT, gpp, ndk and ppa genes, whose products are involved in ppGpp metabolism, was upregulated in PB12 and rpoS inactivation also decreased their transcription, suggesting that sigma38 has a critical role in the expression of these genes in slow growing E. coli cells [11].
###end p 6
###begin title 7
###xml 35 36 35 36 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
Central metabolic routes in the PTS- strains showing key metabolites and the genes involved in their transformation.
###end title 7
###begin p 8
###xml 210 214 210 214 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 214 215 214 215 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 310 313 310 313 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores1">[3]</xref>
###xml 315 319 315 319 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores2">[11]</xref>
PTS, (not shown in the figure) is involved in the wild type strain in glucose transport and phosphorylation, using PEP and producing pyruvate. RTPCR values of these genes in strains JM101, PB11, PB12 and their rpoS- derivatives are shown in the included table. These RTPCR values have been previously reported [3], [11] and are presented in this figure for comparison and discussion purposes. The abbreviations are as follows: glucose (GLC), glucose-6-phosphate (G6P), fructose-6-phosphate (F6P), fructose-1,6-phosphate (F1,6P), dihydroxy-acetone phosphate (DHAP), glyceraldehyde-3-phosphate (G3P), glyceraldehyde-1,3-phosphate (G1,3P), 3-phosphoglycerate (3PG), 2-phosphoglycerate (2PG), phosphoenolpyruvate (PEP), pyruvate (PYR), acetyl-CoA (AcCoA), acetyl phosphate (Ac-P), acetyl-AMP (A-AMP), citrate (CIT), isocitrate (ICT), glyoxalate (Gox), alpha-ketoglutarate (alpha-KG), succinyl-coenzyme A (SUC-CoA), succinate (SUC), fumarate (FUM), malate (MAL), oxaloacetate (OAA).
###end p 8
###begin p 9
###xml 170 174 170 174 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 179 182 179 182 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 216 217 216 217 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 337 341 337 341 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 341 342 341 342 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 575 577 571 573 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 622 624 614 616 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 680 682 668 670 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 778 780 762 764 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 799 801 779 781 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1144 1148 1124 1128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1148 1149 1128 1129 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1273 1280 1253 1260 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1552 1553 1532 1533 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1575 1579 1555 1559 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores3">[28]</xref>
###xml 1581 1585 1561 1565 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-BezViveros1">[31]</xref>
###xml 1587 1591 1567 1571 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Martnez1">[32]</xref>
###xml 1846 1848 1822 1824 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1903 1910 1879 1886 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1273 1280 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1903 1910 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
In this report, we carried out a detailed molecular characterization of the expression of all glycolytic genes and operons and two other central carbon metabolism genes -poxB and acs-, in the wild type and in the PTS- strains by determining their TSSs. This information, and the determination of the TSSs of the same set of genes in the rpoS- derivatives of these strains, allowed us to determine the possible type of promoter(s) controlling their expression. Remarkably, all the genes and operons studied apparently could have more than one promoter. For many of them, sigma70 binding sites and sequences resembling sigma38 recognition elements (also mentioned as "possible sigma38 recognition sites", through this report), were superimposed. The presence of overflapping sigma70 and possible sigma38 recognition sites in these genes, allowed the proposition that they could be transcribed by both sigma subunits from "putative dual promoters", in which transcription initiation, if directed by both sigma factors, occurred at the same site. In some cases, we found differential promoter usage among the studied strains and also between their rpoS- derivatives. The detailed knowledge at the molecular level of the different metabolic strategies for carbon utilization by E. coli strains lacking PTS, will allow a better understanding of the physiology of cells growing slowly on glucose. This information can also be useful in the design of novel metabolic engineering strategies for improving carbon diversion into the aromatic pathway utilizing PTS- strains such as PB12 [28], [31], [32]. Finally, the analysis of this information and other related to the regulation of the glycolytic pathway and to the transformation of pyruvate into AcCoA, allowed the clarification of an important carbon diversion metabolic switch regulated by both sigma38 and pyruvate concentrations that apparently occurs in E. coli strains growing slowly on glucose, at the level of the pyruvate dehydrogenase complex (Pdh) and PoxB to preserve carbon skeletons.
###end p 9

###xml 2865 2886 2849 2870 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and methods</xref>

###xml 2973 2978 2953 2958 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 2978 2981 2958 2961 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Weber1">[5]</xref>
###xml 3037 3039 3013 3015 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 3139 3141 3111 3113 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 3152 3155 3124 3127 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Weber1">[5]</xref>
###xml 3157 3160 3129 3132 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Typas1">[6]</xref>
###xml 3162 3166 3134 3138 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Becker1">[21]</xref>
###xml 3167 3171 3139 3143 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Nystrm1">[23]</xref>
###xml 3276 3278 3244 3246 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 3288 3290 3252 3254 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 3514 3522 3478 3486 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In vitro</italic>
###xml 3801 3805 3765 3769 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 3810 3813 3774 3777 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 116 123 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Here we investigated the promoters directing the expression of the glycolytic and pyruvate decarboxylation genes in E. coli strains growing aerobically on glucose, as the only carbon source (figure 1). Our previous work as well as that of several other groups has provided evidence for a complex regulation of the majority of these genes by both sigma70 and sigma38[3], [7], [11], [30], [31], [33], [34]. However, the molecular details of this control and the type and disposition of the different promoters are still incomplete. In this work, we utilized a modified 5'RACE methodology and a global genomic strategy by pyrosequencing to determine the TSSs, and subsequently the promoters of all these genes in strains JM101, PB11, PB12 and their rpoS- derivative strains. Both methodologies utilized as template total RNA extracted from the cells (Materials and methods, Mendoza et al, submitted to PLoS ONE). In the case of the 5'RACE methodology, we utilized the same RNA that was previously used for quantitative detection of the mRNA of these genes by real time PCR (RTPCR) [3], [11]. For the modified 5'RACE analysis we designed oligonucleotide primers specific for each gene in order to recover from the RNA mixture only those cDNAs of interest, and extended the oligonucleotide primer till the end of the molecule, which normally corresponds to the 5'end of the mRNA. In contrast, the global pyrosequencing strategy does not select for any particular gene and the results obtained normally correspond to the degree of expression of each gene (Mendoza et al, submitted to PLoS ONE). For each gene analyzed by the modified 5'RACE we detected on PAGE at least one band corresponding to the gene-specific amplification product. For some genes we detected also nonspecific PCR products, arising from partial complementarity, coming mainly from the highly abundant rRNAs (Mendoza et al, submitted to PLoS ONE). In several cases, when the intensities of the bands in the gels were weak, DNA bands for the same size were mixed together and sequenced, resulting in the same TSSs. In Materials and methods and Supporting Information sections (figure S1 and table S1), the procedures utilized for cDNA synthesis, separation and sequencing are described in detail. Even when the modified 5'RACE methodology is not quantitative, in several cases the DNA band intensities in the gels correlated with previously reported RTPCR expression values (figure 1) [3], [11], probably because the same RNA was utilized for both experiments; although there were several exceptions. The cDNA bands in the gels were extracted and sequenced up to their 5' end to allow TSSs determinations. Putative sigma70 and sigma38 recognition sequences (table 1) were identified by visual inspection of the DNA sequences upstream the TSSs and by motif finding with the MEME and meta-MEME programs (Materials and methods). The consensus nucleotide sequence of the -10 region for sigma38, described by Weber et al[5], was utilized in this work for detecting possible sigma38 recognition sites. Because the -35 region is less conserved or even absent, especially in the sigma38 promoters [5], [6], [21]-[23], only the -10 region was considered in our analyses. When putative superimposed promoters for both sigma38 and sigma70 were detected sharing the same TSS, an additional number was included in the promoter name to indicate this fact. In those cases we named as mentioned, these two putative overlapping promoters as "putative dual promoters". In vitro transcription experiments and DNA fusions of various promoters to a reporter gene of some of these genes were obtained as additional evidence to support the functionality of these promoters. In the next subsections, the analysis of transcription results for all the glycolytic, poxB and acs genes is presented:
###end p 12

###begin title 16
A) Transcription start site mapping and promoter analysis of glycolytic genes and operons
###end title 16
###begin p 17
###xml 123 127 123 127 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 127 128 127 128 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
In this section, the determination of TSSs and putative promoters for each glycolytic gene in JM101, PB11, PB12, and their rpoS- derivative strains using 5'RACE analysis, is presented.
###end p 17
###begin title 18
###xml 3 6 3 6 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
a) glk
###end title 18
###begin p 19
###xml 117 125 117 125 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 127 131 127 131 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores4">[29]</xref>
###xml 133 137 133 137 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Curtis1">[35]</xref>
###xml 146 148 142 144 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 211 215 207 211 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Meyer1">[36]</xref>
###xml 229 239 225 235 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">figures 2a</xref>
###xml 244 247 240 243 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1a</xref>
###xml 294 297 290 293 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 376 379 372 375 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 476 479 472 475 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 517 521 513 517 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 521 522 517 518 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 538 542 534 538 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 542 543 538 539 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 722 726 718 722 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Meyer1">[36]</xref>
###xml 765 768 761 764 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 811 813 803 805 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 852 854 840 842 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 923 927 911 915 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 927 928 915 916 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 993 996 981 984 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 1159 1162 1147 1150 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 1218 1220 1202 1204 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1321 1325 1305 1309 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1325 1326 1309 1310 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1385 1387 1365 1367 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1428 1431 1408 1411 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 1441 1444 1421 1424 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 1475 1485 1455 1465 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">figures 2a</xref>
###xml 1490 1493 1470 1473 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1a</xref>
###xml 1495 1502 1475 1482 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 1533 1537 1513 1517 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1545 1548 1525 1528 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpo</italic>
###xml 1549 1550 1529 1530 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1619 1622 1599 1602 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 1654 1662 1634 1642 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 1724 1727 1704 1707 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 1764 1766 1740 1742 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1894 1902 1870 1878 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 1904 1907 1880 1883 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores1">[3]</xref>
###xml 1909 1913 1885 1889 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores2">[11]</xref>
This gene codes for glucokinase (Glk), the enzyme that phosphorylates glucose into glucose-6P in the absence of PTS (figure 1) [29], [35]. A sigma70-dependent promoter has previously been reported for this gene [36]. As shown in figures 2a and S1a, there are multiple bands in the gel in which glk TSSs were detected. Only the two smaller ones between 200 and 300 bp produced glk complementary sequences. Nucleotide sequence of the longest of these bands (shown in the gel as glkP1-P2), detected only in PB12 and its rpoS- derivative PB12rpoS- strains, showed that transcription initiated at an A residue, 36 nucleotides upstream the ATG initiation codon. This TSS was one nucleotide longer than a previously reported one [36]. We named this putative dual promoter glkP1-P2 because a sequence resembling a sigma38 recognition element overlaps the sigma70 recognition element (see below). Interestingly, JM101, PB11 and PB11rpoS- strains utilized a different downstream possible dual promoter, glkP3-P4. Nucleotide sequence of the pooled bands from these strains showed that transcription started at a C residue, 21 nucleotides from the ATG initial codon. The glkP3-P4 putative dual promoter does not have a clear sigma70 recognition element but its transcription is apparently dependent on this sigma factor since in the rpoS- strains it was still expressed. Sequences resembling sigma38 recognition sites were detected in both glkP1-P2 and glkP3-P4 putative dual promoters (figures 2a and S1a, table 1). Remarkably, inactivation of rpoS in PB11rpoS- strain apparently enhanced in the gel the amount of transcript from glkP3-P4. RTPCR expression values (figure 1) indicated that in PB11 and in PB12 strains transcription of glk was only slightly dependent on sigma38 been in the limits of the experimental error; nevertheless, transcription of these genes, detected by RTPCR was downregulated (figure 1) [3], [11].
###end p 19
###begin title 20
###xml 40 43 40 43 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 45 48 45 48 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgi</italic>
###xml 50 54 50 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 56 60 56 60 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tpiA</italic>
###xml 62 66 62 66 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gapA</italic>
###xml 68 71 68 71 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">epd</italic>
###xml 76 79 76 79 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 178 199 178 199 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">materials and methods</xref>
Transcription start sites (TSSs) of the glk, pgi, pfkA, tpiA, gapA, epd and pgk glycolytic genes and operons were determined using a modified 5'RACE methodology, as described in materials and methods.
###end title 20
###begin p 21
###xml 644 653 644 653 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">figure S1</xref>
###xml 658 665 658 665 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 733 735 729 731 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 808 813 804 809 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 813 816 809 812 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Weber1">[5]</xref>
###xml 859 861 851 853 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 910 912 898 900 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 973 975 957 959 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1095 1100 1079 1084 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 1100 1104 1084 1088 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Meyer1">[36]</xref>
###xml 1113 1118 1097 1102 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 1118 1122 1102 1106 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Froman1">[37]</xref>
###xml 1142 1146 1126 1130 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Helling1">[39]</xref>
###xml 1160 1165 1144 1149 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 1165 1169 1149 1153 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Charpentier1">[41]</xref>
###xml 1181 1186 1165 1170 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 1186 1190 1170 1174 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Thouvenot1">[43]</xref>
###xml 1199 1204 1183 1188 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 1204 1208 1188 1192 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Bardey1">[45]</xref>
Specific oligonucleotides were designed for each gene in order to recover from the RNA mixture the cDNAs of interest. The cDNAs in the bands were extracted and their nucleotide sequences were determined to their 5'ends to allow TSSs determinations. When multiple PCR bands were present in one gel, these bands were purified and their nucleotide sequences were determined. In some cases, ribosomal or tRNA were detected. In most cases, no specific DNA sequences were obtained indicating nonspecific amplified PCR products (see a precise explanation in the text for each subfigure; the nucleotide sequences of the different cDNA are presented in figure S1 and table 1). The consensus nucleotide sequence of the -10 region for the sigma38 sigma subunit (8 nucleotides, framed in the figures) described by Weber et al[5], was utilized for detecting possible sigma38 recognition sites and a 10 nucleotides -10 sigma70 consensus sequence was utilized for detecting possible sigma70 binding sites. Numbers in parenthesis indicate references in which previously reported TSSs have been described: Meyer et al[36], Froman et al[37], Helling and Evans [39], Charpentier et al[41], Thouvenot et al[43], Bardey et al[45].
###end p 21
###begin title 22
###xml 3 6 3 6 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgi</italic>
b) pgi
###end title 22
###begin p 23
###xml 124 132 124 132 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 142 144 138 140 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 285 289 281 285 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Froman1">[37]</xref>
###xml 303 313 299 309 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">figures 2b</xref>
###xml 318 321 314 317 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1b</xref>
###xml 732 740 728 736 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 742 745 738 741 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores1">[3]</xref>
###xml 747 751 743 747 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores2">[11]</xref>
###xml 753 757 749 753 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores4">[29]</xref>
###xml 816 820 812 816 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 820 821 816 817 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 866 870 862 866 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 870 871 866 867 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 956 958 948 950 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1004 1006 992 994 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1076 1086 1064 1074 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">figures 2b</xref>
###xml 1091 1094 1079 1082 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1b</xref>
###xml 1096 1103 1084 1091 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 1147 1150 1135 1138 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgi</italic>
###xml 1273 1275 1257 1259 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1285 1287 1265 1267 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1322 1325 1302 1305 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgi</italic>
This gene codes for phosphoglucose isomerase (Pgi) an enzyme involved in the transformation of glucose-6P into fructose-6P (figure 1). A sigma70-dependent promoter, which directs transcription starting at an A residue, 36 nucleotides upstream the ATG initiation site has been reported [37]. As shown in figures 2b and S1b, after 5'RACE was performed a single band was detected in all strains. Nucleotide sequences of these bands showed that all initiated at exactly the same position as reported. In PB11 and PB12 strains there was clearly a higher amount of this transcript than in JM101, which is in agreement with the previously reported phosphoglucose isomerase specific activity in PB12 that was 4-5 fold higher than in JM101 (figure 1) [3], [11], [29]. Less amount of transcript was detected in the gel in the rpoS- derivatives as compared to their respective rpoS+ strains, in agreement with reported RTPCR expression values. A possible strong sigma38 recognition -10 element overlapping the sigma70 recognition element was located in the promoter region of this gene (figures 2b and S1b, table 1). This result allowed the proposition that pgi, as it will be seen for other genes below, could be transcribed by these two sigma factors from possible overlapping sigma70 and sigma38 promoters. Therefore, we named it pgiP1-P2 putative dual promoter to indicate that the same TSS could be shared by two different RNAp holoenzymes.
###end p 23
###begin title 24
###xml 3 7 3 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
c) pfkA
###end title 24
###begin p 25
###xml 32 39 32 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 56 59 56 59 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfk</italic>
###xml 67 75 67 75 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 78 82 78 82 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 211 215 211 215 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkB</italic>
###xml 259 263 259 263 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 272 276 272 276 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Frankel1">[38]</xref>
###xml 285 287 281 283 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 361 365 357 361 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 439 443 435 439 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Helling1">[39]</xref>
###xml 457 467 453 463 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">figures 2c</xref>
###xml 472 475 468 471 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1c</xref>
###xml 713 717 709 713 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 717 718 713 714 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 814 818 810 814 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Helling1">[39]</xref>
###xml 857 861 853 857 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 958 962 954 958 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 962 963 958 959 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1404 1412 1400 1408 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 1414 1417 1410 1413 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores1">[3]</xref>
###xml 1419 1423 1415 1419 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores2">[11]</xref>
###xml 1483 1487 1479 1483 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 1560 1564 1556 1560 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1572 1575 1568 1571 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpo</italic>
###xml 1576 1577 1572 1573 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1637 1641 1633 1637 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 1651 1655 1647 1651 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 1723 1725 1715 1717 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1797 1799 1785 1787 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1848 1852 1836 1840 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 1899 1901 1883 1885 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1949 1951 1929 1931 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1994 1998 1974 1978 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 2068 2070 2044 2046 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 2146 2156 2122 2132 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">figures 2c</xref>
###xml 2161 2164 2137 2140 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1c</xref>
###xml 2166 2173 2142 2149 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 2285 2293 2261 2269 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 2315 2319 2291 2295 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 2384 2388 2360 2364 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 2440 2442 2412 2414 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 32 39 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The main phosphofructokinase in E. coli is coded by the pfkA gene (figure 1). pfkA mutants are growth impaired on glucose. However, there is a second minor (10%) phosphofructokinase activity, the product of the pfkB gene. This explains the residual growth of pfkA mutants [38]. A sigma70-dependent promoter has been reported which directs transcription for the pfkA gene initiating at an A residue, 78 nucleotides from the ATG start codon [39]. As shown in figures 2c and S1c, three main bands appeared in the gel in all strains after 5'RACE methodology was performed. The sequence of the uppermost band corresponded to rRNA. The nucleotide sequences of the middle bands, clearly observed in JM101, PB12, and PB12rpoS- showed that in all strains transcription initiated at the same position as previously reported [39]. We named this putative dual promoter pfkAP1-P2 (see below). Very low intensity bands located at the same position in strains PB11 and PB11rpoS- suggests that this promoter was utilized in all strains. The shorter band, which is clearly observed in strain JM101, produced a sequence that started at a C residue, 29 nucleotides from the ATG start codon. Since there were equivalent bands in the other strains it is likely that all of them initiated at this position, although much less efficiently. This low level of expression is in agreement with reported RTPCR transcription values (figure 1) [3], [11]. The latter transcription event was the result of a second pfkAP3-P4 possible dual promoter (see below). Interestingly, inactivation of rpoS in PB11rpoS- decreased transcription from both putative dual promoters (pfkAP1-P2 and pfkAP4-P5), indicating that these promoters could be recognized by sigma38 and could be dual promoters. In fact, a highly consensus possible sigma38 -10 element was located upstream the TSS of the pfkAP1-P2 dual promoter, and another possible sigma38 recognition -10 element that included the sigma70 -10 element, could be also located in the pfkAP3-P4 putative dual promoter; however, in this case the possible sigma38 binding site is located two nucleotides closer to the ATG initiation site (figures 2c and S1c, table 1). Again, the level of transcription of this gene was higher in PB12, as expected from RTPCR expression values (figure 1), and in this strain rpoS inactivation apparently decreased transcription mainly from the pfkAP3-P4 promoter, despite having a poor putative sigma38 recognition sequence.
###end p 25
###begin title 26
###xml 3 7 3 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tpiA</italic>
d) tpiA
###end title 26
###begin p 27
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tpiA</italic>
###xml 136 144 136 144 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 159 169 159 169 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">figures 2d</xref>
###xml 174 177 174 177 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1d</xref>
###xml 274 278 274 278 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tpiA</italic>
###xml 327 331 327 331 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tpiA</italic>
###xml 611 615 611 615 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tpiA</italic>
###xml 663 665 659 661 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 675 677 667 669 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 701 711 693 703 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">figures 2d</xref>
###xml 716 719 708 711 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1d</xref>
###xml 721 728 713 720 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 741 746 733 738 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 746 750 738 742 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Pichersky1">[40]</xref>
###xml 962 966 954 958 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 987 991 979 983 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 991 992 983 984 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1107 1111 1099 1103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1111 1112 1103 1104 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1155 1159 1147 1151 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1159 1160 1151 1152 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1202 1210 1194 1202 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 1274 1276 1262 1264 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
tpiA codes for triosephosphate isomerase (TpiA). This enzyme catalyzes the transformation of dihydroxyacetone-P into glyceraldehyde-3P (figure 1). As shown in figures 2d and S1d, there were two main distinct bands in the gel but only the smallest one, labeled in the gel as tpiAP1-P2, and present in all the strains, came from tpiA. The other band produced an 23S rRNA sequence. Nucleotide sequences of bands from strains JM101, PB11, and PB12 showed the same TSS, not previously reported that initiated at an A residue, 62 nucleotides upstream the ATG start codon. This newly identified putative dual promoter tpiAP1-P2, carried strong overlapping possible sigma70 and sigma38 recognition sequences (figures 2d and S1d, table 1). Pichersky et al[40] predicted a promoter much closer to the ATG that was not detected in our work. Due to the low transcription levels of this gene in the PB11 strain, it was difficult to unambiguously conclude about the effect of rpoS inactivation on PB11rpoS- because of the presence of very small amounts of DNA in the gels. However, less DNA was apparently present in the rpoS- derivatives as compared to their parental rpoS+ strains, in agreement with RTPCR values (figure 1), indicating that transcription of this promoter could be sigma38-dependent.
###end p 27
###begin title 28
###xml 3 7 3 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gapA</italic>
e) gapA
###end title 28
###begin p 29
###xml 42 46 42 46 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gapA</italic>
###xml 120 127 120 127 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 129 137 129 137 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 174 178 174 178 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gapA</italic>
###xml 202 206 202 206 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Charpentier1">[41]</xref>
###xml 268 278 268 278 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">figures 2e</xref>
###xml 283 286 283 286 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1e</xref>
###xml 494 498 494 498 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gapA</italic>
###xml 561 565 561 565 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 565 566 565 566 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 685 695 685 695 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">figures 2e</xref>
###xml 700 703 700 703 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1e</xref>
###xml 744 748 744 748 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gapA</italic>
###xml 769 773 769 773 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Charpentier1">[41]</xref>
###xml 774 778 774 778 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Thouvenot1">[43]</xref>
###xml 811 815 811 815 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 854 857 854 857 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpo</italic>
###xml 858 859 858 859 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 902 905 902 905 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpo</italic>
###xml 906 907 906 907 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 992 1000 992 1000 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 1002 1006 1002 1006 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores2">[11]</xref>
###xml 1034 1037 1034 1037 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgi</italic>
###xml 1042 1046 1042 1046 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tpiA</italic>
###xml 1096 1098 1092 1094 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1136 1138 1128 1130 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1220 1224 1212 1216 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1320 1324 1312 1316 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gapA</italic>
Four promoters have been reported for the gapA gene, which codes for glyceraldehyde-3-phosphate dehydrogenase A (GapA) (table 1, figure 1), and transcription of one of them (gapAP3) is regulated by Crp [41]. 5'RACE experiments resulted in three main bands in the gel (figures 2e and S1e). Attempts to determine the nucleotide sequence of the uppermost did not produce any result, and the smallest band produced a DNA sequence that corresponded to 23S rRNA. The middle one labeled in the gel as gapAP1-P1a, which was clearly present in all strains except in PB11rpoS-, produced sequences pointing to the same TSS that initiated at an A residue, 36 nucleotides from the ATG start codon (figures 2e and S1e). This TSS precisely coincided with the gapAP1 reported promoter [41]-[43]. Interestingly, inactivation of rpoS decreased transcription in strain PB11rpoS-, while it remained constant in strain PB12rpoS- as compared to PB12. These results coincide with published RTPCR expression values (figure 1) [11]. Again, as in the cases of pgi and tpiA, in this DNA region a sequence resembling a sigma38 -10 element, which included the sigma70 -10 reported element, could explain RTPCR results obtained after inactivation of rpoS. Due to previously reported promoters in this gene, this putative dual promoter was labeled as gapAP1-P1a.
###end p 29
###begin title 30
###xml 3 15 3 15 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk and fbaA</italic>
f) pgk and fbaA
###end title 30
###begin p 31
###xml 0 3 0 3 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 8 12 8 12 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fbaA</italic>
###xml 29 41 29 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">epd-pgk-fbaA</italic>
###xml 52 59 52 59 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 141 145 141 145 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Ciria1">[44]</xref>
###xml 147 150 147 150 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 199 203 199 203 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fbaA</italic>
###xml 259 263 259 263 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Frankel1">[38]</xref>
###xml 265 273 265 273 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 384 387 384 387 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">epd</italic>
###xml 512 515 512 515 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">epd</italic>
###xml 554 557 554 557 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 562 566 562 566 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fbaA</italic>
###xml 666 669 666 669 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 675 679 675 679 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Bardey1">[45]</xref>
###xml 699 711 699 711 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">figures 2f-1</xref>
###xml 716 721 716 721 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1f-1</xref>
###xml 745 748 745 748 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">epd</italic>
###xml 857 861 857 861 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Bardey1">[45]</xref>
###xml 907 909 903 905 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 966 969 962 965 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">epd</italic>
###xml 998 1005 994 1001 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 52 59 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
pgk and fbaA are part of the epd-pgk-fbaA operon in E. coli which is conserved in the gamma proteobacteria, as detected by the GeCont Server [44]. pgk codes for the phosphoglycerate kinase (Pgk) and fbaA codes for the fructose-1,6 biphosphate aldolase (FbaA) [38] (figure 1). Two promoters have been reported for this operon; one that transcribes the three genes, located upstream of epd, which initiates transcription 132 nucleotides from the ATG initiation codon and a second one, located at the 3' end of the epd structural gene that transcribes only pgk and fbaA. This latter promoter initiates transcription 235 nucleotides from the ATG initiation codon of the pgk gene [45]. As can be seen in figures 2f-1 and S1f-1 transcription from the epd gene initiated in all strains from the same reported promoter whose expression is controlled by Crp and Cra [45]. Interestingly, a sequence resembling a sigma38 -10 element was detected overlapping this putative dual epdP1-P2 promoter (see below), (table 1).
###end p 31
###begin p 32
###xml 64 67 64 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 72 76 72 76 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fbaA</italic>
###xml 201 205 201 205 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fbaA</italic>
###xml 395 399 395 399 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fbaA</italic>
###xml 586 589 586 589 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 650 662 650 662 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">Figures 2f-2</xref>
###xml 667 672 667 672 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1f-2</xref>
###xml 768 771 768 771 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 778 781 778 781 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 838 845 838 845 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 934 937 934 937 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 996 999 996 999 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 1030 1033 1030 1033 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 1058 1061 1058 1061 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
