###xml 1109 1111 1105 1107 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1149 1152 1145 1148 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 1189 1191 1181 1183 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1252 1264 1244 1256 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">figures 2f-2</xref>
###xml 1269 1274 1261 1266 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1f-2</xref>
###xml 1276 1283 1268 1275 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 1370 1374 1362 1366 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Bardey1">[45]</xref>
###xml 1581 1585 1573 1577 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1621 1624 1613 1616 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">epd</italic>
###xml 1626 1629 1618 1621 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 1634 1638 1626 1630 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fbaA</italic>
###xml 1646 1650 1638 1642 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1650 1651 1642 1643 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1672 1680 1664 1672 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 1781 1785 1773 1777 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1785 1786 1777 1778 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1832 1836 1824 1828 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1836 1837 1828 1829 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 838 845 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
We also investigated the presence of internal promoters between pgk and fbaA because there is a large intergenic region of 214 nucleotides between these two genes. Oligonucleotide primers specific for fbaA were used, but no transcription products were detected, (data not shown), suggesting that there is no promoter immediately upstream of this gene. This result suggests that transcription of fbaA is dependent on the promoters located further upstream in the operon, at least in the growth conditions tested. In order to analyze the possible existence of additional TSSs in front of pgk we designed specific oligonucleotide primers for this gene. Figures 2f-2 and S1f-2, show multiple bands in the gel. The first and third bands from the bottom of the gel label as pgkP2 and pgkP3, were the only ones that rendered sequences from this E. coli region. The other bands did not produce any sequence in multiple attempts utilizing the pgk oligonucleotide primer. The mapped 5'ends of the specific pgk sequences were located at 26 (pgkP2) and 113 nucleotides (pgkP3) from the ATG start codon. A poor sigma sigma70 recognition site was inferred in the pgkP3, but no sequences resembling sigma38 -10 elements were detected in these two proposed promoters (figures 2f-2 and S1f-2, table 1). We did not detect a previously reported TSS located at 235 nucleotides from the ATG [45]. This could be due to different growth conditions used here. Published RTPCR values indicate that transcription levels of these three genes are lower in PB11 and PB12, as compared to JM101. Inactivation of rpoS clearly decreased transcription of epd, pgk and fbaA in the rpoS- derivative strains (figure 1). However, we did not detect any relevant difference in the transcription levels in the gels in the rpoS- derivatives as compared to the corresponding rpoS+ strains.
###end p 32
###begin title 33
###xml 3 7 3 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gpmA</italic>
g) gpmA
###end title 33
###begin p 34
###xml 42 46 42 46 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gpmA</italic>
###xml 108 117 108 117 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g003">figure 3a</xref>
###xml 226 230 226 230 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gpmA</italic>
###xml 400 410 400 410 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g003">figures 3a</xref>
###xml 415 418 415 418 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1g</xref>
###xml 420 427 420 427 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 528 530 524 526 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 554 558 550 554 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Vassinova1">[46]</xref>
###xml 610 613 606 609 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gpm</italic>
###xml 759 768 755 764 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g003">figure 3a</xref>
###xml 802 806 798 802 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 859 863 855 859 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 863 864 859 860 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 918 926 914 922 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 971 975 967 971 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 975 976 971 972 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 998 1006 994 1002 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 1008 1017 1004 1013 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g003">figure 3a</xref>
###xml 1041 1043 1033 1035 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1086 1090 1078 1082 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gpmA</italic>
###xml 1100 1104 1092 1096 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gpmA</italic>
###xml 1135 1145 1127 1137 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g003">figures 3a</xref>
###xml 1150 1153 1142 1145 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1g</xref>
###xml 1155 1162 1147 1154 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
Phosphoglyceromutase A (GpmA) is coded by gpmA. 5'RACE experiments resulted in three main bands in the gel (figure 3a). Attempts to sequence the uppermost band did not produce any result. The lower band, labeled in the gel as gpmAP1-P2, which was clearly present in all strains, produced nucleotide sequences with the same TSS that initiated at an A residue, 37 nucleotides from the ATG start codon (figures 3a and S1g, table 1). This TSS almost coincided (two nucleotides difference), with a proposed TSS from an inferred sigma70 promoter for this gene [46]. The middle band present in all strains labeled as gpmP3-P4, produced sequences with the same TSS in all strains that initiated transcription at an A residue, 75 nucleotides from the ATG start codon (figure 3a). Interestingly, inactivation of rpoS reduced transcription from this band, in strain PB11rpoS- as compared to PB11, in agreement with RTPCR values (figure 1), while there was no apparent effect in PB12rpoS- as compared to PB12 (figure 1, figure 3a). Possible strong sigma38 recognition elements were located in both gpmAP1-P2 and gpmAP2-P3 putative dual promoters (figures 3a and S1g, table 1).
###end p 34
###begin title 35
###xml 40 44 40 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gpmA</italic>
###xml 46 49 46 49 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 51 55 51 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>
###xml 57 61 57 61 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 63 67 63 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pdhR</italic>
###xml 72 76 72 76 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">aceE</italic>
###xml 175 196 175 196 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">materials and methods</xref>
Transcription start sites (TSSs) of the gpmA, eno, pykA, pykF, pdhR and aceE glycolytic genes and operons were determined using a modified 5'RACE methodology, as described in materials and methods.
###end title 35
###begin p 36
###xml 526 535 526 535 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">figure S1</xref>
###xml 540 547 540 547 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 615 617 611 613 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 690 695 686 691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 695 698 691 694 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Weber1">[5]</xref>
###xml 741 743 733 735 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 792 794 780 782 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 855 857 839 841 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 981 986 965 970 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 986 990 970 974 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Vassinova1">[46]</xref>
###xml 1000 1005 984 989 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 1005 1009 989 993 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Shimada1">[47]</xref>
###xml 1029 1033 1013 1017 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Spencer1">[50]</xref>
###xml 1041 1046 1025 1030 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 1046 1050 1030 1034 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Quail1">[51]</xref>
###xml 1063 1068 1047 1052 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 1068 1072 1052 1056 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Cunningham1">[52]</xref>
The cDNAs in the bands were extracted and their nucleotide sequences were determined to their 5'ends to allow TSSs determinations. When multiple PCR bands were present in one gel, these bands were purified and their nucleotide sequences were determined. In some cases, ribosomal or tRNA were detected. In most cases, no specific DNA sequences were obtained indicating nonspecific amplified PCR products (see a precise explanation in the text for each subfigure; the nucleotide sequences of the different cDNA are presented in figure S1 and table 1). The consensus nucleotide sequence of the -10 region for the sigma38 sigma subunit (8 nucleotides, framed in the figures) described by Weber et al[5], was utilized for detecting possible sigma38 recognition sites and a 10 nucleotides -10 sigma70 consensus sequence was utilized for detecting possible sigma70 binding sites. Numbers in parenthesis indicate references in which previously reported TSSs have been described: Vassinova et al[46], Shimada et al[47], Spencer and Guest [50], Quail et al[51], Cunningham et al[52].
###end p 36
###begin title 37
###xml 3 6 3 6 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
h) eno
###end title 37
###begin p 38
###xml 30 33 30 33 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 40 48 40 48 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 72 80 72 80 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pyrG-eno</italic>
###xml 89 99 89 99 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g003">Figures 3b</xref>
###xml 104 107 104 107 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1h</xref>
###xml 264 267 264 267 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 274 277 274 277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 285 288 285 288 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 363 366 363 366 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 478 481 478 481 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 509 512 509 512 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 741 745 741 745 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 756 764 756 764 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PB11rpoS</italic>
###xml 764 765 764 765 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 804 807 804 807 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 878 886 878 886 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 920 922 916 918 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 955 958 951 954 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 968 971 964 967 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 1048 1052 1044 1048 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1123 1128 1119 1124 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 1128 1132 1124 1128 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Shimada1">[47]</xref>
###xml 1390 1392 1382 1384 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1466 1471 1458 1463 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 1471 1475 1463 1467 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Shimada1">[47]</xref>
###xml 1478 1485 1470 1477 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
Enolase (Eno) is coded by the eno gene (figure 1), which is part of the pyrG-eno operon. Figures 3b and S1h show the results of the 5'RACE methodology that consistently produced (four independent experiments), three different extension products labeled in the gel enoP4-P5, enoP6, and enoP7-P8. Transcription from the closest and stronger possible dual promoter (enoP4-P5) (see below), initiated at a T residue, located 27 nucleotides from the ATG initiation codon. The second (enoP6) promoter and the third (enoP7-P8) putative dual promoter (see below), initiated transcription at a T and A residues, located 77 and 212 nucleotides, respectively, from the ATG start codon. Strains PB11 and PB12 utilized the same promoters. Inactivation of rpoS in strain PB11rpoS- slightly decreased transcription from enoP7-P8, in agreement with lower transcription levels detected by RTPCR (figure 1). Sequences resembling poor sigma38 -10 element were located in the enoP7-P8 and enoP4-P5 putative dual promoters; however, as shown in the gel, inactivation of rpoS apparently did not decrease transcription from this promoter. Shimada et al[47], reported three TSSs for this gene with very long 5' untranslated regions initiating at 731, 760, and 903 nucleotides from the ATG. These TSSs were obtained from cells growing in Luria broth, and were not detected in our work. Importantly, no possible sigma38 recognition sequences were detected in the promoters reported by Shimada et al[47], (table 1).
###end p 38
###begin title 39
###xml 3 7 3 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 12 16 12 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>
i) pykF and pykA
###end title 39
###begin p 40
###xml 0 7 0 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 117 125 117 125 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 201 208 201 208 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 243 247 243 247 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Ponce1">[48]</xref>
###xml 581 584 581 584 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Postma1">[1]</xref>
###xml 586 590 586 590 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores4">[29]</xref>
###xml 604 616 604 616 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g003">figures 3c-1</xref>
###xml 621 626 621 626 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1i-1</xref>
###xml 737 741 737 741 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 748 752 748 752 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 760 764 760 764 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 822 826 822 826 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 957 959 953 955 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 969 971 961 963 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 993 997 985 989 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 1173 1174 1165 1166 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1205 1209 1197 1201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 1375 1377 1363 1365 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1415 1416 1403 1404 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1458 1462 1446 1450 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 1503 1504 1491 1492 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1559 1563 1547 1551 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 1623 1627 1611 1615 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 1664 1668 1652 1656 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 1700 1704 1688 1692 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Bledig1">[49]</xref>
###xml 0 7 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 201 208 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
E. coli has isoenzymes to perform some critical metabolic steps. The pyruvate kinases PykA and PykF are one example (figure 1). It has been shown that PykF plays a more significant role than PykA when E. coli is growing aerobically on glucose [48]. Certainly, the conversion of PEP into pyruvate is a very important step that in principle should be finely controlled. Furthermore, in strains lacking PTS, as PB11 and PB12, the pyruvate kinase catalyzed carbon flux from PEP to pyruvate is highly increased probably to compensate for the absence of PTS, the major pyruvate producer [1], [29]. As shown in figures 3c-1 and S1i-1, 5'RACE produced three clear bands in the gel that were the result of promoters not previously reported named pykFP1-P2, pykFP3, and pykFP4-P5, respectively. Transcription from the putative dual pykFP1-P2 promoter that started at a C residue located at 34 nucleotides from the ATG, was high in JM101 and was apparently under sigma70 and sigma38 control (see below). pykFP3 started transcription at a G residue at 80 residues from the ATG and seemed to be specific for JM101 since no bands corresponding to this transcript were detected in the PTS- derivatives. On the contrary, pykFP4-P5, which initiated also at a G residue 97 nucleotides from the ATG, was only detected in these mutant derivatives and also seemed to be highly controlled by sigma38 (see below). Apparently, in these PTS- strains, there was no transcription from pykFP3. These results suggest that in the PTS- strains the utilization of the putative dual promoter pykFP4-P5 is probably inhibiting the use of the closely located pykFP3. A previously predicted promoter (pykFP) was not detected in our work [49].
###end p 40
###begin p 41
###xml 16 20 16 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 52 56 52 56 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 124 128 124 128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 128 129 128 129 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 138 142 138 142 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 142 143 142 143 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 157 165 157 165 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 167 170 167 170 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores1">[3]</xref>
###xml 172 176 172 176 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores2">[11]</xref>
###xml 234 238 234 238 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 261 263 257 259 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 375 377 367 369 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 467 469 455 457 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 560 562 544 546 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 696 697 680 681 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 697 701 681 685 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 701 702 685 686 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 720 724 704 708 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 813 815 793 795 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 878 882 858 862 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 898 910 878 890 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g003">figures 3c-1</xref>
###xml 915 920 895 900 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1i-1</xref>
###xml 922 929 902 909 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 965 969 945 949 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 1041 1045 1021 1025 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 1063 1067 1043 1047 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1067 1068 1047 1048 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1222 1226 1202 1206 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1226 1227 1206 1207 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1250 1258 1230 1238 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 1260 1264 1240 1244 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores2">[11]</xref>
###xml 1293 1297 1273 1277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 1336 1338 1312 1314 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1345 1349 1321 1325 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 1437 1439 1409 1411 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1483 1487 1455 1459 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 1500 1504 1472 1476 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
Inactivation of rpoS clearly decreased the level of pykF transcription detected by RTPCR expression experiments in both PB11rpoS- and PB12rpoS- derivatives (figure 1) [3], [11], in strong agreement with the apparent dependence of the pykFP4-P5 promoter on sigma38, suggesting that this putative dual promoter could be transcribed mainly by this sigma factor but also by sigma70. This interpretation is supported by the presence of a sequence resembling a strong sigma38 -10 recognition element upstream this TSS that also includes a possible superimposed sigma70 -10 element in this putative dual promoter. Interestingly, there was also apparently less transcription as detected in the gel in PTS-rpoS- strains from the pykFP1-P2 putative dual promoter as compared to their parental strains. A possible poor sigma38 -10 recognition element is also present in this putative dual pykFP1-P2 promoter (figures 3c-1 and S1i-1, table 1). In fact, less transcription from pykFP1-P2 was apparently also observed as compared to the one obtained from pykFP3 in strain JM101rpoS- as compared to JM101 (data not shown). This latter result is in agreement with RTPCR values for this gene, where less transcription was detected in JM101rpoS- as compared to JM101 (figure 1) [11]. These results suggest that pykFP3 is not apparently regulated by sigma38 while pykFP1-P2 could be transcribed by both sigma subunits. Nevertheless, no clear possible sigma70 recognition sites were detected neither in pykFP1-P2 nor in pykFP3.
###end p 41
###begin p 42
###xml 12 24 12 24 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g003">figures 3c-2</xref>
###xml 29 34 29 34 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1i-2</xref>
###xml 145 149 145 149 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>
###xml 206 210 206 210 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>
###xml 220 224 220 224 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>
###xml 240 244 240 244 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>
###xml 288 292 288 292 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>
###xml 340 344 340 344 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 344 345 344 345 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 368 369 368 369 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 432 434 428 430 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 632 634 624 626 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 676 680 668 672 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>
###xml 855 859 847 851 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 859 860 851 852 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 892 896 884 888 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 896 897 888 889 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 986 990 978 982 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>
###xml 1024 1032 1016 1024 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 1068 1070 1056 1058 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1138 1150 1126 1138 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g003">figures 3c-2</xref>
###xml 1155 1160 1143 1148 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1i-2</xref>
###xml 1162 1169 1150 1157 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 1238 1242 1226 1230 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 1247 1251 1235 1239 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>
###xml 1331 1332 1319 1320 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
As shown in figures 3c-2 and S1i-2, two main bands and some nonspecific bands of high molecular weight appeared in the transcription analysis of pykA. However, only the two main bands labeled in the gel as pykAP1-P2 and pykAP3-P4, produced pykA specific sequences. Putative dual promoter pykAP1-P2 was clearly expressed in JM101 and in the rpoS- derivatives of the PTS- strains indicating that it was apparently transcribed by sigma70. Interestingly, this transcript that initiated at a C residue, 105 nucleotides from the ATG start codon was apparently as detected in the gel, less expressed in PB11 and PB12, suggesting that sigma38 could also be modulating its expression. pykAP3-P4 that initiated transcription at a G residue, located 153 nucleotides from the ATG start codon, could also be a dual promoter because its expression is diminished in the rpoS- derivatives as compared to the rpoS+ parental strains, in agreement with previously reported reduced transcription levels of pykA by RTPCR expression experiments (figure 1). However, very poor possible sigma38 recognition elements are present in these putative dual promoters (figures 3c-2 and S1i-2, table 1). As it will be discussed later, the differential expression of the pykF and pykA genes, could be the result of different regulatory mechanisms absent in the PTS- strains as compared to JM101.
###end p 42
###begin title 43
###xml 7 21 7 21 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pdhR-aceEF-lpd</italic>
j) The pdhR-aceEF-lpd operon
###end title 43
###begin p 44
###xml 161 169 161 169 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 171 175 171 175 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Frankel1">[38]</xref>
###xml 250 254 250 254 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Spencer1">[50]</xref>
###xml 255 259 255 259 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Cunningham1">[52]</xref>
###xml 352 356 352 356 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">aceE</italic>
###xml 402 405 402 405 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lpd</italic>
###xml 586 589 586 589 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores1">[3]</xref>
###xml 591 595 591 595 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Cunningham1">[52]</xref>
###xml 596 600 596 600 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Liu1">[54]</xref>
This operon codes for the pyruvate dehydrogenase (Pdh) subunits and its transcriptional regulator PdhR. Pdh is involved in the synthesis of AcCoA from pyruvate (figure 1) [38]. Three different promoters for this operon have been previously described [50]-[52]. Interestingly, two of these promoters are within the operon at 48 nucleotides upstream the aceE ATG start codon and 195 nucleotides from the lpd ATG initiation codon. This latter promoter is regulated by ArcA since Lpd is also part of the succinate dehydrogenase complex. Therefore, regulation of this operon is very complex [3], [52]-[54].
###end p 44
###begin title 45
pdhR
###end title 45
###begin p 46
###xml 12 24 12 24 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g003">figures 3d-1</xref>
###xml 29 34 29 34 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1j-1</xref>
###xml 69 73 69 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pdhR</italic>
###xml 283 287 283 287 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Quail1">[51]</xref>
###xml 289 293 289 293 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Cunningham1">[52]</xref>
###xml 354 358 354 358 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pdhR</italic>
###xml 416 420 416 420 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pdhR</italic>
###xml 500 502 496 498 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 512 514 504 506 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 582 584 570 572 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 638 642 626 630 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 642 643 630 631 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 679 683 667 671 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 683 684 671 672 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 797 801 785 789 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 801 802 789 790 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 834 842 822 830 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 887 892 875 880 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 892 895 880 883 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Weber1">[5]</xref>
###xml 942 944 926 928 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
As shown in figures 3d-1 and S1j-1, when the transcripts upstream of pdhR were analyzed we found a single band in all strains. The nucleotide sequence of the DNA generated by 5'RACE extracted from every strain pointed to a TSS that coincided precisely with a previously reported one [51], [52]. This TSS initiated at an A residue 58 nucleotides from the pdhR ATG start codon and we named this putative dual promoter pdhRP1-P2 (see below). Inspection of this promoter region showed possible poor sigma70 and sigma38 recognition elements and it could be partially transcribed by sigma38 since the intensities of the bands in the gel in the rpoS- derivatives were lower than in the rpoS+ parental strains. These data are in agreement with RTPCR expression, because transcription values in strain PB11rpoS- are lower as compared to PB11 (figure 1). In agreement with this observation, Weber et al[5], reported that this gene is regulated by sigma38 and it is overexpressed in several stress conditions.
###end p 46
###begin title 47
aceE
###end title 47
###begin p 48
###xml 52 66 52 66 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pdhR-aceEF-lpd</italic>
###xml 130 134 130 134 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">aceE</italic>
###xml 247 259 247 259 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g003">Figures 3d-2</xref>
###xml 264 269 264 269 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1j-2</xref>
###xml 295 299 295 299 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">aceE</italic>
###xml 575 579 575 579 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">aceE</italic>
###xml 678 682 678 682 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Spencer1">[50]</xref>
###xml 753 757 753 757 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 757 758 757 758 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 768 772 768 772 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 772 773 772 773 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 789 797 789 797 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 864 869 864 869 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">aceEF</italic>
###xml 914 916 910 912 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 991 993 983 985 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1050 1052 1038 1040 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1095 1107 1083 1095 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g003">figures 3d-2</xref>
###xml 1112 1117 1100 1105 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1j-2</xref>
###xml 1119 1126 1107 1114 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
Since there are reported internal promoters for the pdhR-aceEF-lpd operon we decided to investigate possible TSSs in front of the aceE gene. AceE is the E1p component of the pyruvate dehydrogenase complex. This subunit binds the thiamin cofactor. Figures 3d-2 and S1j-2 show a main band labeled aceEP1-P2 in the gel that was present in all strains (the very faint bands in the uppermost part of the gel are nonspecific). The nucleotide sequence of the band from the JM101 strain indicated that the TSS initiated at a G residue, 48 nucleotides from the ATG start codon of the aceE gene. This TSS coincided (one nucleotide difference) with a previously reported one for this gene [50]. According with RTPCR expression values, the transcripts of PB11, PB11rpoS-, and PB12rpoS- were very low (figure 1). These results indicate that transcription of this dual putative aceEF promoter could be under the control of sigma38 and, in fact, as in previous cases, a DNA sequence resembling a poor sigma38 recognition -10 element that includes the reported sigma70 promoter was detected in this DNA region (figures 3d-2 and S1j-2, table 1).
###end p 48
###begin title 49
###xml 46 50 46 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 55 58 55 58 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
B. Transcription start sites determination of poxB and acs genes by 5'RACE
###end title 49
###begin p 50
###xml 259 267 259 267 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 286 290 286 290 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 480 483 480 483 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores1">[3]</xref>
###xml 485 489 485 489 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores5">[30]</xref>
###xml 491 495 491 495 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-AbdelHamid1">[55]</xref>
###xml 532 539 532 539 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 601 604 601 604 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 652 656 652 656 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Kumari1">[56]</xref>
###xml 729 730 729 730 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 730 737 730 737 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 804 807 804 807 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 873 877 873 877 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ackA</italic>
###xml 882 885 882 885 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pta</italic>
###xml 960 963 960 963 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores1">[3]</xref>
###xml 965 969 965 969 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores2">[11]</xref>
###xml 532 539 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 730 737 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Pyruvate oxidase (PoxB) and Acetyl CoA synthase (Acs) constitute an alternative metabolic route to produce acetyl CoA from pyruvate by first oxidizing this metabolite to acetate, producing reducing power at the membrane, and then converting acetate to AcCoA (figure 1). Inactivation of poxB reduces only 5% the growth rate of the wild type strain, but a 50% reduction is observed in the PB11 strain, indicating the critical role that PoxB plays in cells growing slowly on glucose [3], [30], [55]. In addition, it is known that when E. coli cells are growing in low acetate concentrations (< = 10 mM), acs inactivation drastically inhibits their growth [56]. Low acetate concentrations produced by PoxB are probably present in PTS-E. coli cells growing slowly on glucose and this explains upregulation of acs (5-8x) as compared to the wild type, while the expression of the ackA and pta coding for the other acetate producing/incorporating system, is unchanged [3], [11].
###end p 50
###begin title 51
###xml 3 7 3 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
a) poxB
###end title 51
###begin p 52
###xml 39 43 39 43 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">itaE</italic>
###xml 48 52 48 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ybjT</italic>
###xml 96 106 96 106 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g004">Figures 4a</xref>
###xml 111 114 111 114 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1k</xref>
###xml 193 197 193 197 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 221 225 221 225 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 439 443 439 443 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Wise1">[57]</xref>
###xml 508 516 508 516 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 526 530 526 530 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 530 531 530 531 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 554 555 554 555 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 565 574 565 574 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g004">figure 4a</xref>
###xml 657 661 657 661 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 675 677 671 673 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 740 744 736 740 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 744 745 740 741 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 860 862 852 854 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 934 936 922 924 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 973 977 961 965 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Wise1">[57]</xref>
###xml 979 983 967 971 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Chang1">[58]</xref>
###xml 1016 1018 1000 1002 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1126 1130 1110 1114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 1178 1182 1162 1166 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 1310 1314 1294 1298 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
This gene forms part of an operon with itaE and ybjT, which is conserved in the Enterobacteria. Figures 4a and S1k show the amplified PCR products obtained with an oligonucleotide specific for poxB. A major band, labeled poxBP1-P2 in the gel, was clearly observed in all strains. Sequence analysis showed that the TSSs initiated at a G residue, 27 nucleotides upstream the ATG start site of this gene; the same TSS was previously reported [57]. As expected from previous expression levels detected by RTPCR (figure 1), in the rpoS- derivatives of the PTS- strains (figure 4a), these transcripts were less abundant, which indicate a strong dependence of the poxB gene on sigma38. However, there was still some transcription occurring in the rpoS- strains. As shown above for many glycolytic genes, the expression was also apparently partially dependent on sigma70. The DNA region upstream of this TSS has a consensus sequence for sigma38, which has been previously reported [57], [58], as well as an overlapping sigma70 -10 recognition element that was identified in this study. Therefore, we named this putative dual promoter poxBP1-P2. A second band of lower intensity labeled poxBP3 in the gel, was detected mainly in strains PB11 and PB12. Nucleotide sequence of this shorter band located this TSS into the poxB structural gene, 20 nucleotides downstream the ATG initiation codon. We do not know the functionality of this promoter.
###end p 52
###begin title 53
###xml 40 44 40 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 49 52 49 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 128 149 128 149 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">materials and methods</xref>
Transcription start sites (TSSs) of the poxB and acs genes were determined using a modified 5'RACE methodology, as described in materials and methods.
###end title 53
###begin p 54
###xml 191 200 191 200 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">figure S1</xref>
###xml 205 212 205 212 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 279 281 275 277 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 353 358 349 354 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 358 361 354 357 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Weber1">[5]</xref>
###xml 404 406 396 398 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 455 457 443 445 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 518 520 502 504 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 639 644 623 628 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 644 648 628 632 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Wise1">[57]</xref>
###xml 656 661 640 645 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 661 665 645 649 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Chang1">[58]</xref>
###xml 674 679 658 663 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 679 683 663 667 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Kumari2">[60]</xref>
###xml 696 701 680 685 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 701 705 685 689 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Beatty1">[61]</xref>
The cDNAs in the bands were extracted and their nucleotide sequences determined to their 5'ends to allow TSSs determinations. The nucleotide sequences of the different cDNA, are presented in figure S1 and table 1. The consensus nucleotide sequence of the -10 region for the sigma38 sigma subunit (8 nucleotides framed in the figures) described by Weber et al[5], was utilized for detecting possible sigma38 recognition sites and a 10 nucleotides -10 sigma70 consensus sequence was utilized for detecting possible sigma70 binding sites. Numbers in parenthesis indicate references in which previously reported TSSs have been described: Wise et al[57], Chang et al[58], Kumari et al[60], and Beatty et al[61].
###end p 54
###begin title 55
###xml 3 6 3 6 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
b) acs
###end title 55
###begin p 56
###xml 41 45 41 45 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yjcH</italic>
###xml 50 54 50 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">actP</italic>
###xml 67 74 67 74 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 74 78 74 78 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Gimenez1">[59]</xref>
###xml 146 150 146 150 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Ciria1">[44]</xref>
###xml 152 156 152 156 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yjcH</italic>
###xml 204 208 204 208 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">actP</italic>
###xml 256 266 256 266 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g004">Figures 4b</xref>
###xml 271 274 271 274 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1l</xref>
###xml 345 346 345 346 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 367 370 367 370 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 693 698 693 698 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 698 702 698 702 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Kumari2">[60]</xref>
###xml 1234 1239 1234 1239 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 1239 1243 1239 1243 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Beatty1">[61]</xref>
###xml 1317 1324 1317 1324 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 1352 1360 1352 1360 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 1528 1531 1528 1531 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 1630 1631 1630 1631 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1763 1766 1763 1766 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 1782 1783 1782 1783 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1793 1801 1793 1801 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 1942 1946 1942 1946 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Kumari2">[60]</xref>
###xml 2004 2012 2004 2012 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 2045 2046 2045 2046 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 2046 2050 2046 2050 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 2050 2051 2050 2051 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 2091 2092 2091 2092 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 2121 2124 2121 2124 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 2266 2268 2262 2264 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 2278 2280 2270 2272 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 2282 2292 2274 2284 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g004">figures 4b</xref>
###xml 2297 2300 2289 2292 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1l</xref>
###xml 2302 2309 2294 2301 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 67 74 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
This gene is the first of an operon with yjcH and actP, present in E. coli[59] and several other Enterobacteria, as detected by the GeCont Server [44]. yjcH codes for a protein of unknown function, while actP, interestingly, codes for an acetate permease. Figures 4b and S1l, show the product of the cDNA amplification as a mayor band in the PTS- strains, labeled as acsP2-P3 in the gel. As observed for other analyzed genes, there were high molecular weight nonspecific bands that did not produce DNA sequence. In strains PB11 and PB12, the TSSs determined from the bands obtained from the gel, initiated at a C residue, located 20 nucleotides from the ATG start codon. Interestingly, Kumari et al[60], inferred two TSSs based on the presence of binding sites for the regulatory Fnr and CRP proteins. The shorter one coincides precisely with the one mapped here. The second longer one could be one of the bands detected in the uppermost part of the gel. However, as we mentioned above, the DNA bands that appeared in the gels mainly in strains JM101 and PB11 at approximately 400 nucleotides were carefully analyzed but no DNA sequence was obtained. Therefore, we cannot confirm the existence of the other predicted promoter. Beatty et al[61], constructed mutants of the putative promoters and analyzed their effect in vivo by promoter fusions and by in vitro transcription experiments. They concluded that both promoters are functional and the closest one, the same detected here, is the one responsible for the major part of acs expression. It is very interesting that this promoter as expected, was highly expressed in the PTS- strains as compared with JM101. We have also observed in RTPCR expression experiments a 5 to 8 times enhanced transcription of the acs gene in the PTS- strains (figure 1). These observations are consistent with the expected catabolite repression of acetate utilization in the wild type when growing on glucose [60]. Since the expression of this gene as detected by RTPCR (figure 1), was clearly reduced in the PTS-rpoS- strains as compared to the parental PTS- strains, we classified this acsP2-P3 also as a putative dual promoter. Sequence upstream of the TSS showed clear overlapping strong possible recognition sites for both sigma38 and sigma70 (figures 4b and S1l, table 1).
###end p 56
###begin title 57
C. Confirmation of several of the detected TSSs by 5'RACE in a global TSS mapping experiment and additional evidence that supports the functionality of the proposed promoters
###end title 57
###begin p 58
###xml 80 87 80 87 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 147 152 147 152 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 228 233 228 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">aceEF</italic>
###xml 239 242 239 242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lpd</italic>
###xml 342 349 342 349 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 369 372 369 372 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgi</italic>
###xml 379 383 379 383 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 390 394 390 394 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gapA</italic>
###xml 401 404 401 404 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">epd</italic>
###xml 414 418 414 418 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gpmA</italic>
###xml 540 543 540 543 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 550 554 550 554 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 561 565 561 565 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tpiA</italic>
###xml 572 575 572 575 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 579 582 579 582 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 589 593 589 593 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>
###xml 603 607 603 607 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 656 660 656 660 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 683 691 683 691 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g005">figure 5</xref>
###xml 80 87 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
In a global transcription initiation mapping by pyrosequencing of the wild type E. coli strain MG1665 more than 1500 TSSs were determined (Mendoza et al, submitted to PLoS ONE). Transcripts from all the glycolytic genes (except aceEF, and lpd), were detected in this genomic experiment. Twelve TSSs were exactly the same as those reported in table 1, from these, five (pgiP1-P2, pfkAP1-P2, gapAP1P1a, epdP1-P2 and gpmAP1-P2) had previously been reported or inferred, and seven corresponded to new proposed promoters described in this work (glkP3-P4, pfkAP3-P4, tpiAP1-P2, pgkP3, enoP4-P5, pykAP3-P4 and pykFP1-P2). As an example, the TSSs detected for the pfkA gene are presented in figure 5.
###end p 58
###begin title 59
###xml 46 50 46 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
This figure shows the TSSs determined for the pfkA gene in an independent global transcription initiation mapping experiment in which random primers were utilized instead of specific oligonucleotides.
###end title 59
###begin p 60
###xml 88 93 88 93 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 322 326 322 326 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 332 336 332 336 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Helling1">[39]</xref>
###xml 537 541 537 541 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 624 628 624 628 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 669 678 669 678 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">figure 2c</xref>
As can be seen in this experiment in which more than 1500 TSSs were determined (Mendoza et al, submitted to PLoS ONE), there are four of these transcripts that initiated at the same nucleotide A (78 nucleotides from the initiation ATG codon). This nucleotide has been reported as the transcription initiation site for the pfkA gene [39]. In addition, transcription also occurred in several cases from another site that initiated with a T residue, (29, nucleotides from the ATG start codon). It has been shown that transcription from the pfkAP1-P2 promoter is responsible for the previously reported transcription event and, pfkAP3-P4 is responsible for a second event (figure 2c).
###end p 60
###begin p 61
###xml 0 8 0 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In vitro</italic>
###xml 202 205 202 205 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgi</italic>
###xml 207 211 207 211 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gapA</italic>
###xml 213 217 213 217 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pdhR</italic>
###xml 222 225 222 225 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 243 245 239 241 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 255 257 247 249 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 294 302 286 294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 307 310 299 302 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgi</italic>
###xml 317 321 309 313 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gapA</italic>
###xml 329 333 321 325 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pdhR</italic>
###xml 343 346 335 338 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 432 436 424 428 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 441 445 433 437 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>
###xml 455 463 447 455 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 512 516 504 508 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 523 527 515 519 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 534 538 526 530 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>
###xml 548 552 540 544 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>
###xml 591 595 583 587 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 634 642 626 634 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 680 684 672 676 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>
###xml 752 756 744 748 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 787 795 779 787 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 808 810 796 798 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 892 900 880 888 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 914 923 902 911 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g006">figures 6</xref>
###xml 928 930 916 918 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s002">S2</xref>
In vitro transcription experiments demonstrated that several of the proposed putative dual promoters were transcribed by both sigma subunits. For example, in the cases of genes with one detected TSS as pgi, gapA, pdhR and acs genes, both sigma38 and sigma70 subunits recognized and transcribed in vitro the pgiP1-P2, gapAP1-P1a, pdhRP1-P2 and acsP2-P3 putative dual promoters. The same was true for genes with more than one TSSs as pykF and pykA in which in vitro transcription from both putative dual promoters pykFP1-P2, pykFP4-P5, pykAP1-P2 and pykAP3-P4 was detected. In the case of the pfkA gene in which two TSSs were detected, in vitro transcription occurred only from the pykAP1-P2 putative dual promoter by both sigma factors. Remarkably, the poxB promoter was only transcribed in vitro by the sigma38 subunit. Importantly, the same TSSs identified by 5'RACE, were detected in these in vitro experiments (figures 6 and S2).
###end p 61
###begin title 62
###xml 0 8 0 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In vitro</italic>
###xml 55 57 51 53 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 68 70 60 62 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
In vitro transcription from several promoters by Esigma70 and Esigma38.
###end title 62
###begin p 63
###xml 128 130 124 126 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 140 142 132 134 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 285 287 273 275 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
