###xml 298 300 282 284 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 328 332 312 316 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 367 375 351 359 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 384 386 364 366 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 588 592 568 572 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Grainger1">[24]</xref>
###xml 967 976 947 956 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s002">figure S2</xref>
###xml 981 1002 961 982 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and methods</xref>
The figure shows scans of denaturing 5% polyacrylamide gels of transcriptions generated by RNA polymerase (E) with either Esigma38 or Esigma70, from supercoiled pSR plasmids carrying different promoters. As can be seen in all the gels, all the promoters were transcribed by both Esigma70 and Esigma38, with the exception of the poxB promoter which is not transcribed in vitro by sigma70. Different intensities indicate varying binding capacities. In all the gels the presence of a plasmid pSR correspondent RNA-I transcript produced with both sigmas, was detected, as previously reported [24]. The expression of this RNA-I was utilized as an internal control, since as expected in all the experiments was present. The sizes of the transcripts and the nucleotide sequences of the DNA fragments carrying these promoters corresponded to the expected for each promoter. Similar results were obtained in duplicate gels for several of the analyzed genes. (For details, see figure S2 and Materials and methods).
###end p 63
###begin p 64
###xml 64 67 64 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgi</italic>
###xml 69 73 69 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 75 79 75 79 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tpiA</italic>
###xml 81 84 81 84 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 90 93 90 93 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 288 291 288 291 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgi</italic>
###xml 298 302 298 302 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tpiA</italic>
###xml 309 313 309 313 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 320 323 320 323 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 331 334 331 334 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 401 404 401 404 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cat</italic>
###xml 463 464 463 464 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">r</sup>
###xml 503 524 503 524 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and methods</xref>
###xml 529 538 529 538 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s003">figure S3</xref>
###xml 831 832 831 832 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">r</sup>
###xml 883 892 883 892 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s003">figure S3</xref>
###xml 894 901 894 901 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 401 404 <span type="species:ncbi:9685">cat</span>
The functionality of some of the proposed putative promoters in pgi, pfkA, tpiA, pgk, and eno, genes was also demonstrated by fusion of DNA fragments carrying some of these promoters to a reporter gene. DNA fragments carrying the "closest to the ATG initiation codon proposed promoters" (pgiP1-P2, tpiAP1-P2, pfkAP3-P4, pgkP2, and enoP4-P5) of these genes, were constructed and cloned in front of the cat reporter gene which confers chloramphenicol resistance (Cmr) present in the plasmid PKK232-8 (see Materials and methods and figure S3). Cells carrying recombinant plasmids were selected for their growth on chloramphenicol. The correct sequence of the cloned DNA segments carrying the different promoters, were verified by gel electrophoresis and nucleotide sequences of the cloned fragments. All these constructions allowed Cmr, indicating the functionality of these promoters (figure S3, table 1).
###end p 64
###begin p 65
###xml 155 159 155 159 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gpmA</italic>
###xml 166 169 166 169 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 173 176 173 176 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 183 187 183 187 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 194 198 194 198 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">aceE</italic>
###xml 205 212 205 212 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
In conclusion, transcription from all the putative proposed promoters reported here by 5'RACE, has been confirmed by at least one other method, except for gpmAP3-P4, enoP6, enoP7-P8, pykFP3 and aceEP1-P2 (table 1).
###end p 65
###begin title 66
###xml 34 36 30 32 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 90 97 86 93 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 90 97 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
2. The roles of pyruvate and sigma38 in carbon flux diversion during carbon limitation in E. coli
###end title 66
###begin p 67
###xml 5 12 5 12 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 296 298 292 294 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 383 387 379 383 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 392 395 388 391 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 460 463 456 459 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Weber1">[5]</xref>
###xml 465 468 461 464 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Typas1">[6]</xref>
###xml 470 473 466 469 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Hua1">[8]</xref>
###xml 475 479 471 475 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores2">[11]</xref>
###xml 481 485 477 481 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Ferenci2">[15]</xref>
###xml 487 491 483 487 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores5">[30]</xref>
###xml 5 12 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
When E. coli is growing slowly on glucose due to low concentrations of this sugar or by PTS inactivation, the genes coding for alternative glucose transport and phosphorylation such as MglB, GalP and Glk are upregulated. In these nutrient scavenging stress conditions, the expression of the sigma38 modulon that includes the upregulation of several central metabolism genes, such as poxB and acs, is induced, thus modifying the strategy for carbon utilization [5], [6], [8], [11], [15], [30]. In these conditions PoxB is responsible for pyruvate oxidation, reducing the role of Pdh for pyruvate decarboxylation (see below).
###end p 67
###begin p 68
###xml 73 87 73 87 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pdhR-aceEF-lpd</italic>
###xml 259 263 259 263 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Quail1">[51]</xref>
###xml 583 588 583 588 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">aceEF</italic>
###xml 730 734 730 734 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-McFall1">[62]</xref>
###xml 783 787 782 786 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 787 788 786 787 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 825 829 824 828 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 829 830 828 829 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 844 851 843 850 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t002">table 2</xref>
###xml 919 926 918 925 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1004 1006 999 1001 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1078 1082 1073 1077 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pdhR</italic>
###xml 1193 1195 1184 1186 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1300 1307 1291 1298 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1766 1769 1757 1760 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores1">[3]</xref>
###xml 1771 1775 1762 1766 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores2">[11]</xref>
###xml 1777 1781 1768 1772 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores5">[30]</xref>
###xml 1783 1791 1774 1782 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 919 926 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1300 1307 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
In the wild type strain growing fast on glucose the complete Pdh operon (pdhR-aceEF-lpd) is expressed as a polycistronic mRNA, because in these growing conditions the concentration of pyruvate is relatively high, and therefore, there is no repression by PdhR [51]. However, in strains growing slowly on glucose, such as PB11, where the glycolytic flux is reduced, pyruvate concentration is also reduced allowing PdhR to repress transcription of its own promoter, with the subsequent decrease in the transcription of the Pdh operon. This proposal explains higher RTPCR values for the aceEF genes in JM101 as compared to PB11, and the result that alanine addition to the growing medium, which can rapidly be converted into pyruvate [62], increased substantially the mu of PB11 and PB11rpoS- strains but not that of PB12 or PB12rpoS-, as shown in table 2. These results, as will be discussed in detail, indicate that when E. coli cells are growing slowly on glucose or in other non optimal conditions, sigma38 as the general regulatory stress modulator, performs the regulation of pdhR. If low pyruvate concentration is present, this reduces transcription of the Pdh operon. Simultaneously, sigma38 induces the synthesis of PoxB which is in charge of pyruvate oxidation in stress conditions. Therefore, E. coli cells growing slowly on glucose apparently reduce carbon flux through the Pdh system which yields directly AcCoA from pyruvate, and increase the flux through the PoxB enzyme that produces acetate and reducing power at the membrane from pyruvate. Acetate, as part of the gluconeogenic metabolism, is incorporated through Acs as AcCoA into the gluconeogenic "carbon preserving-recycling" metabolism that is present in strain PB11 which grows slowly on glucose [3], [11], [30] (figure 1).
###end p 68
###begin title 69
###xml 43 45 42 44 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 87 91 86 90 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 95 96 94 95 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">r</sup>
Specific growth rate determinations (mu = h-1) for the PB11 and PB12 strains and their rpoS::Tcr derivatives.
###end title 69
###begin p 70
Alanine was added at a final concentration of 0.5 g/l.
###end p 70

###end title 71
###begin p 72

###xml 1307 1311 1283 1287 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>

###xml 1375 1377 1343 1345 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>

###xml 1564 1576 1528 1540 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">epd-pgk-fbaA</italic>
###xml 1683 1686 1647 1650 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">epd</italic>
###xml 1726 1727 1690 1691 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1871 1874 1835 1838 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pox</italic>
###xml 1880 1883 1844 1847 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 1940 1944 1904 1908 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 1975 1977 1935 1937 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 2042 2046 2002 2006 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 2225 2227 2181 2183 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 2293 2295 2245 2247 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 2310 2313 2262 2265 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 2374 2376 2322 2324 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 2376 2379 2324 2327 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 2408 2412 2356 2360 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 2412 2413 2360 2361 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 2531 2533 2475 2477 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 2603 2605 2543 2545 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 2651 2653 2587 2589 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 2693 2696 2629 2632 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 2913 2915 2845 2847 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
In this work, several TSSs and proposed promoters of all glycolytic genes and operons as well as two other central carbon metabolism genes involved in the transformation of glucose into AcCoA, were identified by a modified 5'RACE strategy and confirmed by pyrosequencing; a total of 17 genes were analyzed. It has been published that in the PTS- strain PB11 which grows slowly on glucose, the transcription level of all glycolytic genes is reduced when rpoS was inactivated, indicating that their expression was partially controlled by sigma38[11]. The evidence presented in this work strongly supports the proposal that in genes with previously reported sigma70 promoters (glkP1-P2, pgiP1-P2, pfkAP1-P2, epdP1-P2, gapAP1-P1a, pdhRP1-P2 and aceEP1-P2), transcription could occur from two overlapping or putative dual promoters in each gene that included both sigma70 recognition sites and possible sigma38 binding sites, in which transcription initiation if directed by both sigma factors, occurred at the same site in all strains. Additionally, new possible sigma70 and sigma38 dependent putative dual promoters were described in this report for other glycolytic genes, (glkP3-P4, pfkAP3-P4, tpiAP2-P3, pgkP2, pgkP3, gpmAP1-P2, gpmAP3-P4, enoP4-P5, enoP6, enoP7-P8, pykFP1-P2, pykFP3, pykP4-P5, pykAP1-P2, pykAP3-P4), in which possible sigma70 and sequences resembling sigma38 recognition sites were also overlapped in most of them. No sequences resembling sigma38 recognition sites were found neither in pgk nor in fbaA. However, these two genes are part of the epd-pgk-fbaA operon and RTPCR data indicate that these three genes could be transcribed by both sigma factors from the epdP1-P2 putative dual promoter, in the PTS- strains. PoxB and Acs play an important role in carbon metabolism in the convertion of pyruvate into AcCoA in cells growing slowly on glucose. poxB and acs, also could have putative dual promoters. We found that poxB is mainly transcribed by sigma38 from the previously reported promoter; however, inactivation of rpoS did not abolish its transcription, in agreement with RTPCR results, indicating that this could also be dual promoter. Again, as for many glycolytic genes, a strong putative sigma70 recognition sequence was detected overlapping this reported sigma38 promoter. The acs gene was mainly transcribed by its originally proposed sigma70acsP2 promoter. However, in the rpoS- derivative strains its expression, as detected by RTPCR, was reduced, implying that could be also controlled by sigma38. In agreement with this observation, we found a possible strong sigma38 recognition element superimposed to the sigma70 promoter integrating the putative dual acsP2-P3 promoter. The experiments presented here, in agreement with RTPCR values indicate that in strain PB11, at least one of the putative dual promoters described for each gene or operon, could be transcribed by sigma38.
###end p 72
###begin p 73
###xml 131 134 131 134 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">epd</italic>
###xml 181 185 181 185 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>
###xml 278 281 278 281 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 493 497 493 497 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tpiA</italic>
###xml 623 627 623 627 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 629 632 629 632 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 637 640 637 640 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 887 890 887 890 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 894 897 894 897 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 901 904 901 904 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 911 914 911 914 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
The majority of the TSSs detected in this work lay within the first 100 nucleotides upstream the ATG initiation codons, except for epd that initiated transcription 132 nucleotides, pykA in which two TSSs were located at 105 and 153 nucleotides, and for one of the three TSSs in eno that initiated 212 nucleotides upstream the ATG initiation codon. Remarkably, for those genes with previously reported promoters mapped less than 100 nucleotides from the ATG, we found the same TSSs (except for tpiA). On the other hand, for promoters previously described further apart of the ATG start codon (more than 100 nucleotides), as pykF, eno and pgk, we did not find transcription from these sites; instead we detected new promoters for all of these genes located within the first 100 nucleotides upstream the ATG codon. It is important to mention that some of the previously reported promoters (enoP1, enoP2, enoP3 and pgkP1) not detected in this report, were described in other metabolic conditions (growing on Luria broth), suggesting differential expressions from these promoters.
###end p 73
###begin p 74
###xml 193 197 193 197 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gpmA</italic>
###xml 204 207 204 207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 299 301 295 297 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 341 343 333 335 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 471 473 459 461 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 483 485 467 469 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1359 1361 1339 1341 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1472 1476 1452 1456 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1476 1477 1456 1457 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1516 1520 1496 1500 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1520 1521 1500 1501 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1621 1628 1601 1608 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1730 1735 1710 1715 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al</italic>
###xml 1843 1846 1823 1826 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgi</italic>
###xml 1853 1857 1833 1837 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 1864 1868 1844 1848 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gapA</italic>
###xml 1876 1879 1856 1859 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">epd</italic>
###xml 1889 1893 1869 1873 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gmkA</italic>
###xml 1946 1949 1926 1929 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 1956 1960 1936 1940 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 1967 1971 1947 1951 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tpiA</italic>
###xml 1978 1981 1958 1961 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 1985 1988 1965 1968 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 1995 1999 1975 1979 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 2010 2014 1990 1994 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>
###xml 2045 2048 2025 2028 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgi</italic>
###xml 2055 2059 2035 2039 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 2066 2070 2046 2050 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tpiA</italic>
###xml 2077 2080 2057 2060 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 2088 2091 2068 2071 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 2114 2117 2094 2097 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cat</italic>
###xml 2182 2190 2162 2170 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 2288 2290 2264 2266 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 2300 2302 2272 2274 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 2352 2359 2324 2331 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 1621 1628 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 2114 2117 <span type="species:ncbi:9685">cat</span>
The existence and functionality of these new putative dual promoters is supported by the following results: a) most of the previously experimentally determined TSSs and two inferred promoters (gpmAP1 and acsP2) coincided with the ones obtained here, b) the presence of DNA sequences resembling sigma38 recognition sites overlapping the sigma70 binding sites in all these genes, allowed the proposition that these genes could be transcribed from overlapping putative sigma38 and sigma70 promoters, defined as putative dual promoters, c) TSSs for most of the genes identified by 5'RACE were mapped in five, and in some cases six different strains. The same results were consistently obtained. In several cases, when the intensities of the bands in the gels were very weak, DNA bands of the same size from different strains were mixed together and sequenced, resulting in the same single TSS. For the majority of the analyzed genes two or more independent experiments were performed, obtaining identical results, d) two different methods for labeling the cDNA ends were employed: polyhomonucleotide tail incorporation and oligonucleotide ligation (developed for cDNA library construction in pyrosequencing, but also used to assess the results of the 5'RACE TSSs mapping), and both methodologies were coincident, e) in most of the genes, the inactivation of sigma38 reduced the amount of transcript detected in the gel (in agreement with RTPCR values), in at least one of the rpoS- strains as compared to their parental rpoS+ strains, f) a global transcription initiation mapping experiment by pryrosequencing of a different E. coli K12 strain, in which random primers were utilized instead of gene-specific oligonucleotides (Mendoza et al, submitted to PLoS ONE), provided independent evidence for the existence of five previously reported TSSs (pgiP1-P2, pfkAP1-P2, gapAP1-P1a, epdP1-P2 and gmkAP1-P2) and seven TSSs mapped in this work by 5'RACE (glkP3-P4, pfkAP3-P4, tpiAP1-P2, pgkP3, enoP4-P5, pykFP1-P2, and pykAP3-P4), g) promoter fusions of pgiP1-P2, pfkAP3-P4, tpiAP1-P2, pgkP2, and enoP4-P5, with a reporter cat gene, demonstrated the functionality of these DNA sequences, h) in vitro transcription experiments for several genes demonstrated that they were transcribed by both sigma38 and sigma70, and produced the same TSSs as the ones detected in vivo.
###end p 74

###xml 318 322 302 306 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Grainger1">[24]</xref>

###xml 1364 1368 1320 1324 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1368 1369 1324 1325 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1426 1435 1382 1391 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figures 1</xref>
###xml 1440 1442 1396 1398 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g004">4a</xref>
###xml 1470 1472 1422 1424 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1498 1506 1450 1458 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 1570 1578 1522 1530 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 1872 1879 1824 1831 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 1964 1971 1916 1923 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 2055 2057 2003 2005 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 2067 2069 2011 2013 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 2164 2171 2108 2115 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 2176 2184 2120 2128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 2208 2211 2152 2155 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Weber1">[5]</xref>
sigma70 and sigma38 are very similar proteins and in fact genes whose transcription is sigma70 dependent in vivo can often be transcribed in vitro by sigma38 and vice versa However, in vitro transcription has been extensively used as evidence to support the expression capability of different sigma subunits [4], [5], [24]. We utilized this technique to generate additional important evidence to support the functionality of the proposed putative promoters. In vitro transcription of promoters with one detected TSS as pgi, gapA, acs and pdhR, or with more than one as pykFP1-P2, pykFP3-P4, pykAP1-P2 and pykAP3-P4 was performed by both sigma subunits (figures 6 and S2), even when DNA sequences resembling very poor sigma70 and sigma38 recognition sites were present in the pdhRP1-P2, pykAP1-P2 and pykAP3-P4 putative dual promoters. Transcription of the poxB gene clearly occurred in vitro when sigma38 was utilized, in agreement with the fact that a strong sigma38 recognition sequence is present in this promoter, but not by sigma70, despite the fact that there is also a sigma70 recognition element in this dual promoter (figure 4a, table 1). Nevertheless, the results obtained in this report demonstrated that this putative dual promoter was transcribed in vivo by sigma70 in the PTS-rpoS- strains where transcription is clearly reduced as compared to their rpoS+ parental strains, but the promoter is still functional (figures 1 and 4a). It is not clear why sigma70 was unable to transcribe in vitro this promoter. Importantly, the same TSSs were detected in the in vitro transcription experiments as those reported by 5'RACE, supporting the fact that obtained 5'RACE results are real and not the result of processing. These results also indicate that both sigma subunits are apparently capable of recognizing their binding sites and produce the same transcript as in vivo, supporting the proposition that these putative dual promoters could be transcribed in vivo by both sigma subunits. It is important to emphasize, as mentioned that since sigma70 and sigma38 are very similar proteins this situation could allow the recognition of similar binding sites in vivo and in vitro, in certain conditions [5].
###end p 75
###begin p 76
###xml 60 64 60 64 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 69 72 69 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 132 134 128 130 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 144 146 136 138 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 322 324 310 312 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 429 431 413 415 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 712 716 696 700 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 779 783 763 767 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 783 784 767 768 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 893 894 877 878 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 924 928 908 912 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 928 929 912 913 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 962 966 946 950 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 966 967 950 951 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1080 1082 1060 1062 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1110 1112 1086 1088 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1193 1195 1165 1167 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1407 1409 1375 1377 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1419 1421 1383 1385 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1485 1487 1445 1447 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1497 1499 1453 1455 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1509 1518 1465 1474 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">figures 2</xref>
###xml 1520 1521 1476 1477 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g003">3</xref>
###xml 1526 1527 1482 1483 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g004">4</xref>
###xml 1529 1536 1485 1492 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 1720 1724 1676 1680 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Bronwning1">[63]</xref>
Remarkably, all glycolytic genes and operons as well as the poxB and acs genes could have functional putative overlapping dual sigma70 and sigma38 promoters, whose positions are at the typical distance from the TSSs. A possible differential utilization of these two sigma factors correlates with carbon availability: sigma38 plays a major role in the expression of these genes in carbon deprivation stress conditions, while sigma70 is mainly used when cells are growing under carbon surplus conditions. This interpretation, as it will be explained below in more detail, is supported by two additional facts to those previously described in this discussion: 1) the observation that, as mentioned, inactivation of rpoS decreased transcription of all glycolytic genes in strain PB11rpoS- as detected previously by RTPCR, and 2) its inactivation reduced also the growth rate in carbon deprived PTS- strains, particularly in PB11rpoS-, but also to some extend in PB12rpoS- which as expected, is less stressed. Wild type JM101 growing exponentially on glucose is less dependent on sigma38. The functionality of sigma38 apparently could also hold for several genes previously reported as having sigma70 promoters, indicating that their expression could be indeed also partially controlled by the former sigma factor. Several of these putative dual promoters have possible strong recognition elements for both sigma38 and sigma70, while others have possible weaker elements also for both sigma38 and sigma70 factors (figures 2, 3 and 4, table 1). However, it is known that other factors such as DNA structure or interaction with transcriptional regulators, influence the ability of sigma factors to recognize weak binding sites [63]. As it will be discussed below in detail, transcription plasticity, understanded as the capacity of a gene to be transcribed by more than one sigma factor, could have been selected, to allow permanent transcription of the genes involved in the transformation of glucose-6P into pyruvate in different metabolic conditions; remarkably, many of these genes work also as gluconeogenic and their expression is controlled by few general transcriptional regulators. Following, a comparative analysis of the proposed promoters is presented.
###end p 76
###begin title 77
Comparative and detailed analysis of the identified proposed promoters
###end title 77
###begin p 78
###xml 15 18 15 18 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 64 67 64 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 77 80 77 80 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 153 155 149 151 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 175 179 171 175 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Froman1">[37]</xref>
###xml 267 274 263 270 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 312 314 304 306 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 324 326 312 314 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 431 435 419 423 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 533 542 521 530 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figures 1</xref>
###xml 547 549 535 537 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">2a</xref>
###xml 551 558 539 546 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 693 696 681 684 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 813 816 801 804 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores1">[3]</xref>
###xml 818 822 806 810 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores5">[30]</xref>
###xml 860 863 848 851 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 897 901 885 889 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 901 902 889 890 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 972 976 960 964 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1127 1129 1111 1113 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1241 1245 1225 1229 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1245 1246 1229 1230 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1487 1490 1471 1474 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 1626 1627 1610 1611 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1906 1909 1890 1893 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Hua1">[8]</xref>
###xml 1911 1915 1895 1899 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Ferenci2">[15]</xref>
###xml 2077 2080 2061 2064 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores1">[3]</xref>
###xml 2457 2458 2441 2442 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 2458 2462 2442 2446 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 2462 2463 2446 2447 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 2497 2501 2481 2485 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 2501 2502 2485 2486 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 2521 2529 2505 2513 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 2551 2554 2535 2538 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 2564 2567 2548 2551 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 2621 2623 2601 2603 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 2633 2635 2609 2611 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
In the case of glk in which two TSSs were identified by 5'RACE: glkP1-P2 and glkP3-P4; the former, found in PB12, has been previously reported as a sigma70 dependent promoter [37], while the latter used by strains JM101 and PB11, was also detected by pyrosequencing (table 1). DNA sequences resembling poor sigma38 and sigma70 recognition elements were detected in these putative dual promoters of this gene, where inactivation of rpoS, apparently increased transcription in the gel from the reported promoters, as detected by PAGE (figures 1 and 2a, table 1). The use of a different promoter in PB12, as compared to JM101 and PB11, could be partially responsible for the higher (2x) level of glk transcription detected by RTPCR that correlates with higher (2x) Glk specific activity in PB12 as compared to JM101 [3], [30]. Increased transcription levels from glkP1-P2 detected in the gels in PB12rpoS- that do not in agree with RTPCR values; if real, could indicate that rpoS inactivation increased the transcription levels from this putative dual promoter, by allowing a more efficient transcription of this promoter by sigma70. The same type of phenomenon could explain the apparent increase in transcription levels in the gel of the PB11rpoS- strain as compared to PB11 that are also not in agreement with RTPCR values. However, it should be taken into account that 5'RACE is not a quantitative methodology and this could explain these differences. It is important to point out that glk is one of the few glycolytic genes whose transcription was not reduced as detected by RTPCR in strain PB11 as compared to JM101. In PTS- strains, and probably in wild type strains growing very slowly on glucose, Glk is the enzyme that phosphorylates transported glucose into glucose-6P. Interestingly, the transcription of this gene was upregulated in a wild type strain grown on glucose as carbon limited nutrient [8], [15]. Nevertheless, it is remarkable that in this gene in which no mutation occurred neither in its regulatory nor in its structural regions in strains PB11 and PB12 [3], apparently two different TSSs are present, indicating that transcription plasticity could allow the utilization of more than one promoter in different metabolic conditions. Apparently, all glycolytic genes could have more than one promoter, supporting this transcription plasticity proposal (see below). The fact that transcription is reduced as detected by RTPCR in both PTS-rpoS- derivatives as compared to their rpoS+ parental strains (figure 1), suggests that both glkP1-P2 and glkP3-P4 could work as dual promoters recognized by sigma38 and sigma70.
###end p 78

###xml 79 82 79 82 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgi</italic>

###xml 249 252 249 252 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>

###xml 391 394 391 394 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">epd</italic>
###xml 457 459 453 455 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 518 520 510 512 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 537 539 525 527 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 617 620 605 608 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">epd</italic>
###xml 625 629 613 617 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pdhR</italic>
###xml 673 677 661 665 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 717 719 701 703 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 721 730 705 714 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">figures 2</xref>
###xml 732 733 716 717 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g003">3</xref>
###xml 738 739 722 723 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g004">4</xref>
###xml 741 748 725 732 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 852 860 836 844 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 890 893 874 877 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgi</italic>
###xml 895 899 879 883 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gapA</italic>
###xml 901 905 885 889 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pdhR</italic>
###xml 910 913 894 897 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 961 965 945 949 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 987 995 971 979 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 1004 1006 984 986 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1008 1017 988 997 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g006">figures 6</xref>
###xml 1022 1024 1002 1004 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s002">2S</xref>
###xml 1026 1033 1006 1013 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
In the case of genes with only one detected TSS by 5'RACE methodology, such as pgi, tpiA, gapA, epd (first promoter of the epd-pgk-fbaA operon), pdhR (first promoter of the pdhR-aceEF-lpd operon), aceEF (internal promoter of this operon), poxB, and acs, rpoS inactivation reduced the amount of transcription in these genes as detected by RTPCR and gel electrophoresis (with the exception of epd in the gel), suggesting that they are at least partially sigma38-dependent. As mentioned, possible overlapping strong sigma70 and strong sigma38 -10 recognition elements were detected in these genes (with the exception of epd and pdhR). However, all these promoters (except for poxB) seem to be mainly transcribed by sigma70 (figures 2, 3 and 4, table 1). Transcription from several promoters of this group of genes was also detected by pyrosequencing, and in vitro transcription confirmed that pgi, gapA, pdhR and acs were transcribed by both sigma subunits, while poxB was only transcribed in vitro by sigma38 (figures 6 and 2S, table 1).
###end p 79
###begin p 80
###xml 15 18 15 18 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 93 96 93 96 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pkf</italic>
###xml 99 103 99 103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gmkA</italic>
###xml 105 108 105 108 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 110 113 110 113 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pyk</italic>
###xml 119 122 119 122 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pyk</italic>
###xml 125 134 125 134 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">figures 2</xref>
###xml 139 140 139 140 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g003">3</xref>
###xml 142 149 142 149 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 237 241 237 241 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 308 310 304 306 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 310 314 306 310 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores2">[11]</xref>
###xml 316 324 312 320 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 407 409 399 401 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 419 421 407 409 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 561 563 545 547 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 573 575 553 555 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
In addition to glk, there are other genes in which 5'RACE detected two or three TSSs such as pkfA, gmkA, eno, pykF and pykA (figures 2 and 3, table 1). Transcription levels of several of these genes was reduced as detected by RTPCR when rpoS was inactivated, suggesting that they could be recognized by sigma38[11] (figure 1). This proposition is supported by the presence of putative overlapping dual sigma38 and sigma70 recognition elements located upstream of the TSSs of several of these putative dual promoters; in all the cases, possible overlapping sigma70 and sigma38-10 recognition elements were present, as it is discussed below:
###end p 80
###begin p 81
###xml 15 19 15 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 27 29 23 25 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 58 61 54 57 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfk</italic>
###xml 166 169 162 165 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfk</italic>
###xml 223 232 219 228 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">figure 2c</xref>
###xml 344 352 340 348 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g005">figure 5</xref>
###xml 354 361 350 357 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 378 380 370 372 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 390 392 378 380 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 473 477 461 465 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 519 521 503 505 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 596 600 580 584 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 717 721 701 705 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 742 746 726 730 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 746 747 730 731 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 841 850 825 834 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figures 1</xref>
###xml 852 854 836 838 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">2c</xref>
###xml 856 863 840 847 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 880 884 864 868 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 906 914 890 898 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 939 947 923 931 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g006">figure 6</xref>
In the case of pfkA a sigma70dependent promoter part of a pfkAP1-P2 putative dual promoter has previously been reported. In this gene a second putative dual promoter pfkAP3-P4 utilized in the three strains, was identified (figure 2c). In addition, the same two TSSs were detected for this gene by pyrosequencing supporting their functionality (figure 5, table 1). Possible sigma70 and sigma38 overlapping recognition elements were found in both putative dual promoters; in pfkAP1-P2 a sequence resembling a strong sigma38 recognition sequence was detected, whereas a poor one was detected in the pfkAP3-P4 putative dual promoter. The proposition that both could be dual promoters is supported by the observation that rpoS inactivation in PB11rpoS- decreased transcription as compared to PB11 as detected by gel electrophoresis and by RTPCR (figures 1, 2c, table 1). However, only pfkAP1-P2 was transcribed in vitro by both sigma subunits (figure 6).
###end p 81
###begin p 82
###xml 7 11 7 11 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gpmA</italic>
###xml 46 50 46 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gpmA</italic>
###xml 60 64 60 64 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gpmA</italic>
###xml 86 95 86 95 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g003">figure 3a</xref>
###xml 117 121 117 121 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gpmA</italic>
###xml 164 171 164 171 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 234 238 234 238 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 277 281 277 281 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 281 282 281 282 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 297 301 297 301 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gpmA</italic>
###xml 312 316 312 316 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gpmA</italic>
###xml 423 425 419 421 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 435 437 427 429 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 504 508 496 500 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gpmA</italic>
###xml 521 525 513 517 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gpmA</italic>
###xml 572 576 564 568 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gapA</italic>
###xml 581 584 573 576 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 602 606 594 598 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 714 718 706 710 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 718 719 710 711 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 793 795 781 783 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 965 973 953 961 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
In the gpmA gene, two putative dual promoters gpmAP1-P2 and gpmAP3-P4 were described (figure 3a). Transcription from gpmAP1-P2 was also detected by pyrosequencing (table 1). Apparently, in agreement with RTPCR values, inactivation of rpoS decreased transcription in strain PB11rpoS- at least from gpmAP3-P4. For gpmAP1-P2 in this strain transcription seemed unchanged in the gel; however, possible strong superimposed sigma38 and sigma70recognition elements were detected in both putative dual promoters gpmAP3-P4 and in gpmAP1-P2. Interestingly, in this gene and also in gapA and eno, inactivation of rpoS did not have any effect neither in the RTPCR value nor in the transcription level on the gel of strain PB12rpoS- as compared to PB12. These results suggest a more important role of sigma70 in the transcription of these promoters in this strain with higher glycolytic flux, where RTPCR values were enhanced as compared to the parental strains JM101 and PB11 (figure 1).
###end p 82
###begin p 83
###xml 52 64 52 64 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">epd-pgk-fbaA</italic>
###xml 109 112 109 112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">epd</italic>
###xml 188 198 188 198 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">figures 2f</xref>
###xml 203 206 203 206 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1f</xref>
###xml 208 215 208 215 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 234 238 234 238 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 289 293 289 293 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 293 294 293 294 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 336 344 336 344 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 390 392 386 388 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 455 457 447 449 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 524 527 516 519 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">epd</italic>
###xml 570 581 562 573 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">figure 2f-1</xref>
###xml 583 590 575 582 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 645 648 637 640 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 698 700 686 688 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 745 748 733 736 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 755 758 743 746 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 781 792 769 780 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g002">figure 2f-2</xref>
###xml 827 830 815 818 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 874 877 862 865 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 930 933 918 921 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cat</italic>
###xml 940 949 928 937 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s003">figure S3</xref>
###xml 951 958 939 946 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 1029 1032 1017 1020 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgk</italic>
###xml 1037 1041 1025 1029 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fbaA</italic>
###xml 1237 1240 1225 1228 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">epd</italic>
###xml 1343 1347 1331 1335 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1401 1402 1389 1390 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1412 1420 1400 1408 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 930 933 <span type="species:ncbi:9685">cat</span>
As mentioned earlier, transcription of the complete epd-pgk-fbaA operon initiated in all strains at the same epdP1-P2 putative dual promoter; repeated experiments confirmed these results (figures 2f and S1f, table 1). Inactivation of rpoS decreased transcription of all these genes in the rpoS- derivative strains as detected by RTPCR (figure 1); in agreement, a sequence resembling a sigma38 recognition element was located overlapping the reported sigma70 recognition site of this promoter. Notice that transcription from epdP1-P2 was also detected by pyrosequencing (figure 2f-1, table 1). Two additional TSSs were detected by 5'RACE for the pgk gene. Nevertheless, no sequences resembling sigma38 recognition elements were detected in these pgkP2 and pgkP3 putative promoters (figure 2f-2). Importantly, transcription from pgkP3 was also detected by pyrosequencing, and pgkP2 was able to promote transcription of the reporter cat gene (figure S3, table 1). In addition, no TSSs were detected in the intergenic region between pgk and fbaA. These results not only suggest that transcription of this last gene occurred from upstream promoters in this operon, but also that these three genes are apparently transcribed from the putative epdP1-P2 dual promoter, as a polycistronic mRNA in the analyzed growing conditions, since inactivation of rpoS decreased transcription of all three genes in the PTS- strains (figure 1).
###end p 83
###begin p 84
###xml 51 54 51 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 199 202 199 202 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 209 212 209 212 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 219 222 219 222 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 229 239 229 239 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g003">figures 3b</xref>
###xml 244 247 244 247 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s001">S1h</xref>
###xml 249 256 249 256 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 293 296 293 296 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 385 388 385 388 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cat</italic>
###xml 395 404 395 404 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s003">figure S3</xref>
###xml 406 413 406 413 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 432 436 432 436 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 501 505 501 505 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 505 506 505 506 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 607 610 607 610 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 635 636 635 636 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 635 640 635 640 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sup>&#8722;</sup>rpoS</italic>
###xml 640 641 640 641 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 693 696 693 696 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eno</italic>
###xml 798 800 794 796 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 820 829 816 825 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g003">figure 3b</xref>
###xml 831 838 827 834 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 385 388 <span type="species:ncbi:9685">cat</span>
Three different new transcription products for the eno gene were detected in several independent 5'RACE experiments. We have labeled the proposed promoters responsible for these expression events as enoP4-P5, enoP6 and enoP7-P8 (figures 3b and S1h, table 1). Importantly, the same TSS for the enoP4-P5 was found by pyrosequencing, and this promoter was able to transcribe the reporter cat gene (figure S3, table 1). Inactivation of rpoS decreased transcription from this gene especially in strain PB11rpoS- as detected by RTPCR. Transcription levels in the gels were slightly reduced from the putative dual enoP7-P8 promoter in the PTS-rpoS- strains, but not apparently from the putative dual enoP4-P5 promoter. Interestingly, these two putative dual promoters carry sequences resembling poor sigma38 recognition sites (figure 3b, table 1). Again, as in several other cases, it is important to emphasize that 5'RACE is not a quantitative methodology.
###end p 84
