###xml 1508 1512 1488 1492 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1512 1513 1492 1493 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1552 1553 1532 1533 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1548 1553 1528 1533 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1555 1563 1535 1543 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 1594 1596 1570 1572 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1635 1639 1611 1615 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 1649 1653 1625 1629 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 1879 1883 1855 1859 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 1904 1908 1880 1884 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Bledig1">[49]</xref>
###xml 2213 2252 2189 2228 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Bledig1">[49, Regulon DB http://www.ccg.unam.mx]</xref>
###xml 2363 2365 2335 2337 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 2526 2530 2498 2502 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Bronwning1">[63]</xref>
###xml 2546 2550 2518 2522 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 2560 2564 2532 2536 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 2599 2601 2567 2569 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 2719 2723 2687 2691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 2723 2724 2691 2692 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 2877 2881 2845 2849 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 2891 2895 2859 2863 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 2931 2933 2895 2897 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 2950 2952 2910 2912 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 3021 3029 2981 2989 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 3091 3095 3051 3055 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 3105 3109 3065 3069 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 3186 3190 3146 3150 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 3233 3242 3193 3202 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g006">figures 6</xref>
###xml 3247 3249 3207 3209 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s002">S2</xref>
###xml 3251 3258 3211 3218 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 3383 3390 3343 3350 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 3538 3539 3498 3499 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 3552 3556 3512 3516 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 3610 3614 3570 3574 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>
###xml 3383 3390 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
In the case of pykF, three different putative promoters pykFP1-P2, pykFP3 and pykFP4-P5 were described. Inactivation of rpoS apparently decreased transcription levels in the gel of the two putative dual promoters pykFP1-P2 and pykFP4-P5 that were functional in the PTS- strains (figure 3c-1). Expression from pykFP4-P5 was not observed in the wild type strain. This putative dual promoter has strong overlapping possible sigma38 and sigma70 -10 recognition elements. In this gene, transcription was performed in the three strains from the three different putative promoters. However, while in all the strains transcription from pykFP1-P2 was detected, transcription from pykFP3 was only observed in the wild type strain. Metabolic conditions in PTS- strains allowed transcription mainly from the pykFP4-P5 apparently sigma38-dependent promoter, probably inhibiting the utilization of the closely located pykP3 that is functional in the wild type strain. Remarkably, transcription levels determined by RTPCR were slightly diminished in both PTS- strains as compared to JM101 (figure 1). This could be explained by high transcription levels apparently occurring from the pykFP4-P5 putative dual promoter in the PTS- strains as shown in the gel. No clear sequences resembling sigma70 recognition elements were found neither in pykFP1-P2 nor in pykFP3. However, a sequence resembling a very poor sigma38 recognition element present in pykFP1-P2 could explain lower transcription levels from this promoter in the rpoS- derivative strains including JM101rpoS- (figure 1).The absence of distinct sigma70 -10 recognition elements upstream the pykFP1-P2 and pykFP3 putative promoters allows the speculation that the two transcripts seen in the gel corresponding to these two promoters could be specific processing or degradation products from a larger mRNA produced from the non detected pykFP predicted promoter [49]. However, no transcription was detected from this predicted promoter even when using oligonucleotides designed to prime closer to it, ruling out its expression at least in these growing conditions (data not shown). Cra, which recognition site is located 197 nucleotides upstream the ATG initiation codon [49, Regulon DB http://www.ccg.unam.mx] or some other factor, could play a role in the utilization of these putative promoters in which no clear sigma70 -10 recognition elements were detected. As mentioned, certain factors can facilitate transcription of promoters with poor or no obvious sigma recognition sites [63]. Nevertheless, pykFP4-P5 and pykFP1-P2 could be transcribed by sigma38 since inactivation of this sigma factor reduced transcription in the gel of these two putative dual promoters in the rpoS- derivative strains. These experiments suggest that they could be real promoters and, as mentioned, the wild type strain transcribed this gene from both pykFP1-P2 and pykFP3 promoters in the absence of sigma38, such that sigma70 is apparently controlling their expression in this strain. In fact, in vitro transcription indicates that the two putative dual promoters pykFP1-P2 and pykFP4-P5 are recognized by both sigma factors and transcription initiation from pykFP1-P2 has been detected by pyrosequencing (figures 6 and S2, table 1). Therefore, these two putative dual promoters seem to be functional in these strains. It is important to emphasize that in E. coli strains lacking PTS, the absence of this general regulator increases the carbon flux through the PykA and PykF enzymes, and apparently in these PTS- strains the pykF gene seems to be preferentially transcribed from the pykF4-P5 putative dual promoter, which is not functional in the wild type strain when growing exponentially on glucose.
###end p 85

###xml 1472 1476 1452 1456 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykF</italic>

###xml 1761 1765 1729 1733 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Bronwning1">[63]</xref>

###xml 2217 2221 2185 2189 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pkyA</italic>
###xml 2358 2362 2326 2330 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>
###xml 2491 2495 2459 2463 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>
###xml 2531 2535 2499 2503 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pykA</italic>
###xml 2676 2679 2644 2647 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>
###xml 2805 2813 2773 2781 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 2856 2859 2824 2827 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pgi</italic>
###xml 2861 2865 2829 2833 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gapA</italic>
###xml 2867 2871 2835 2839 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pfkA</italic>
###xml 2873 2877 2841 2845 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tpiA</italic>
###xml 2879 2883 2847 2851 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pdhR</italic>
###xml 2885 2889 2853 2857 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">aceE</italic>
In pykA, two putative dual promoters were detected in the three strains by 5'RACE. Clearly, these two promoters were transcribed in JM101 indicating that sigma70 is performing this expression. While inactivation of rpoS apparently decreased transcription in the gel from pykAP3-P4 putative dual promoter in PB12rpoS- and possibly in PB11rpoS-, it is interesting that this inactivation apparently increased transcription in the gel from pykAP1-P2 in both PTS- strains (figure 3c-2). The same type of phenomenon of increased transcription detected in the gel for two promoters occurred in glk. Importantly, both pykA promoters have DNA sequences resembling poor sigma70 -10 recognition elements and also DNA sequences resembling very poor sigma38 recognition sequences. However, inactivation of rpoS markedly decreased transcription levels (more than 50%) of pykA in both PTS-rpoS- strains as compared to their respective parental rpoS+ derivatives, as detected by RTPCR (figure 1), suggesting an important role of this sigma factor in the expression of pykA. In fact, in vitro transcription demonstrated that both putative dual promoters are transcribed by sigma38 and sigma70 (figures 6 and S2). Remarkably, in vitro transcription of these two putative dual pykA promoters by both sigma fagctors, rendered weaker bands than those corresponding to other promoters, including the one in the plasmid responsible for RNA-I. These results suggest, as has been proposed for the pykFP1-P2 promoter in which a DNA sequence resembling a poor sigma70 recognition site is present that in vivo some other factor could play a role in the utilization of these pykA putative dual promoters where DNA sequences resembling weak sigma70 and sigma38 recognition sites are present [63]. Transcription from the putative pykAP3-P4 dual promoter has also been detected by pyrosequencing. Interestingly, higher RTPCR values were present in the transcription of this gene in PB12 as compared to PB11, while the same transcription level was exhibited in both strains in the pykF gene as detected by RTPCR. Therefore, it is possible that during the selection of PB12 for growth recovery on glucose the transcription of several genes, including pkyA was upregulated as compared to PB11, increasing in turn the glycolytic carbon flux. Clearly, there is a differential utilization of the pykA promoters in strain PB12 as compared to PB11. Apparently, this latter strain utilizes preferentially the putative dual promoter pykAP1-P2 whereas PB12 transcription of pykAP3-P4 is highly increased in comparison to the parental PB11 strain. Differential utilization of promoters is also apparently present in the glk gene and clearly upregulation of the expression of most glycolytic genes in PB12, as compared to PB11, as revealed by RTPCR (figure 1) is also detected in several other genes (pgi, gapA, pfkA, tpiA, pdhR, aceE) in the gels. These results could explain in part, faster growth of PB12 over PB11.
###end p 86

###xml 318 329 314 325 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g003">figure 3d-1</xref>
###xml 420 422 412 414 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 432 434 420 422 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 492 494 476 478 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 523 527 507 511 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pdhR</italic>
###xml 527 530 511 514 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Weber1">[5]</xref>
###xml 532 536 516 520 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Quail1">[51]</xref>
###xml 552 560 536 544 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 703 712 687 696 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g006">figures 6</xref>
###xml 717 719 701 703 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0007466.s002">2S</xref>
###xml 721 728 705 712 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 765 767 745 747 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 791 793 767 769 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 925 929 901 905 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pdhR</italic>
###xml 982 987 958 963 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">aceEF</italic>
###xml 1134 1138 1110 1114 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Quail1">[51]</xref>
###xml 1212 1216 1188 1192 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">aceE</italic>
###xml 1254 1258 1230 1234 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Spencer1">[50]</xref>
###xml 1330 1332 1302 1304 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1342 1344 1310 1312 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1397 1399 1361 1363 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1409 1411 1369 1371 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 1451 1455 1411 1415 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1455 1456 1415 1416 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1483 1487 1443 1447 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 1487 1488 1447 1448 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1562 1566 1522 1526 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pdhR</italic>
###xml 1589 1597 1549 1557 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g001">figure 1</xref>
###xml 1683 1686 1643 1646 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Weber1">[5]</xref>
###xml 1731 1736 1691 1696 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">aceEF</italic>
###xml 1882 1885 1842 1845 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Weber1">[5]</xref>
###xml 1988 1992 1948 1952 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pdhR</italic>
###xml 2047 2052 2007 2012 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">aceEF</italic>
###xml 2074 2081 2034 2041 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 2090 2093 2050 2053 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Weber1">[5]</xref>
###xml 2109 2113 2069 2073 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pdhR</italic>
###xml 2269 2273 2229 2233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pdhR</italic>
###xml 2327 2331 2287 2291 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Spencer1">[50]</xref>
###xml 2333 2337 2293 2297 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Quail1">[51]</xref>
###xml 2074 2081 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
In all strains, transcription of the pdhR-aceEF-lpd operon initiated at the same pdhRP1-P2 putative dual promoter, upstream of pdhR. In derivative strains lacking sigma38, not only transcription levels of pdhR were diminished, as seen from the RTPCR values (figure 1), but also the intensity of the bands in the gels (figure 3d-1). These results suggest that this promoter region may include functional overlapping sigma70 and sigma38 promoters and are in agreement with the report that sigma38 modulates the expression of pdhR[5], [51]. As mentioned, in vitro transcription provided additional evidence to support the fact that both sigma subunits recognize and transcribe this putative dual promoter (figures 6 and 2S, table 1). Interestingly, possible poor sigma70 and possible poor sigma38 overlapping recognition sites are present in this putative dual promoter. Independently from the results concerning the TSS in the pdhR gene, the data presented here also indicate that an aceEF internal putative dual promoter is apparently functional in all strains, and may work as a constitutive promoter because PdhR does not repress it [51]. This is in agreement with the result that in all strains the TSS at the aceE gene coincided with the reported one [50]. Again, transcription from this DNA region carrying both possible sigma70 and sigma38 superimposed boxes apparently depended on both sigma70 and sigma38 and transcription was decreased in PB11rpoS- and more evidently in PB12rpoS- strains, as compared to their parental strains. Finally, upregulation of pdhR was detected in PB12 (figure 1) and in another wild type strain grown on Luria broth in different stress conditions [5]. However, less upregulation was detected in aceEF (1.4x) in PB12 whereas no upregulation of these two genes was reported in a wild type strain grown on Luria broth in different stress conditions [5]. These results indicate that a transcription termination mechanism could be present at the end of the pdhR structural gene allowing lower upregulation values of aceEF in PB12 and in other E. coli strains [5] as compared to pdhR, since these genes are mainly transcribed as part of a polycistronic mRNA. In this regard, a possible terminator sequence has been described at the end of pdhR structural gene that could explain these differences [50], [51].
###end p 87

###xml 1660 1667 1624 1631 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>

###xml 1867 1875 1831 1839 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0007466-g006">figure 6</xref>
###xml 1911 1913 1871 1873 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 2051 2055 2011 2015 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>
###xml 2060 2063 2020 2023 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acs</italic>
###xml 2139 2141 2095 2097 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 2151 2153 2103 2105 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 2216 2223 2168 2175 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 2282 2283 2234 2235 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 2605 2607 2553 2555 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 2617 2619 2561 2563 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 2635 2642 2579 2586 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0007466-t001">table 1</xref>
###xml 2718 2720 2658 2660 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 2730 2732 2666 2668 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">38</sup>
###xml 2981 2984 2917 2920 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Weber1">[5]</xref>
###xml 2986 2989 2922 2925 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Typas1">[6]</xref>
###xml 2991 2995 2927 2931 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Lengeler1">[16]</xref>
###xml 2997 3001 2933 2937 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Grainger1">[24]</xref>
###xml 3003 3007 2939 2943 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Bronwning1">[63]</xref>
###xml 2216 2223 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Our results show that rpoS inactivation decreased transcription in several previously reported sigma70-dependent promoters in glycolytic genes and operons: pgiP1-P2, pfkAP1-P2, gapAP1-1a, epdP1-P2, pdhRP1-P2, aceEP1-P2. In fact, in these six genes which have the same reported transcription initiation sites and are mainly transcribed by sigma70, six new proposed putative sigma38 promoters superimposed to sigma70 recognition sequences, were described in these putative dual promoters. Several of these new possible sigma38 sites are strong recognition sequences. In addition, new dual putative promoters were described: tpiAP2-P3, pykFP1-P2, pykFP4-P5, pykAP1-P2, pykAP3-P4 and possibly glkP1-P2, glkP3-P4, pfkAP3-P4, gpmAP1-P2, gpmAP3-P4, enoP4-P5, and enoP7-P8 that all seem to include both sigma70 and sigma38 superimposed possible recognition elements. Importantly, some of these putative dual promoters in this last group carry DNA sequences resembling poor sigma38 recognition sequences especially pykFP1-P2, pykAP1-P2, pykAP3-P4, pfkAP3-P4, and enoP7-P8 (figures 2 and 3, table 1). However, inactivation of rpoS in strain PB11rpoS- reduced the transcription levels of all these genes detected by RTPCR, suggesting, as previously mentioned that at least one of the putative dual promoters in each gene or operon could be transcribed by sigma38 (figure 1). In addition, the independent global transcription mapping experiment allowed the identification by pyrosequencing of the same TSSs detected for twelve of these proposed dual promoters, and fusion of chromosomal DNA fragments carrying one or more of these promoters to a reporter gene (figure S3, table 1), corroborated the functionality of some of these promoters. Finally, in vitro experiments confirmed that several proposed dual promoters are transcribed in these experiments by both sigma subunits (figure 6). These results indicate that sigma38 plays a central role in the regulation of all glycolytic genes and operons and at least in two other important central metabolism genes -poxB and acs- that could be at the transcription level since possible superimposed sigma70 and sigma38 putative dual promoters were detected in all these genes when E. coli cells were grown slowly on glucose, as occurred in the PTS- strains, specially in PB11. The presented results allowed the identification of fourteen new TSSs by 5'RACE and the proposal of more than 30 putative promoter sequences in 17 central metabolism genes and operons not previously described. The majority of these putative promoter sequences could be recognized by both sigma38 and sigma70 sigma factors (table 1). Certainly as mentioned, some of these putative promoters carry poor sigma70 and sigma38 binding sites. If these promoters are real and they are transcribed by both sigma subunits, other factors such as DksA, Crl, Cra, Fis, H-NS and IHF, could modulate the binding capacities and selectivities of these sigma subunits in these promoters [5], [6], [16], [24], [63].
###end p 88

###xml 85 86 85 86 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>

Alternative scenarios that could also explain the low transcription levels in the PTS-rpoS-

###xml 2581 2585 2537 2541 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Sigala1">[64]</xref>

###xml 2865 2868 2817 2820 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glk</italic>

###xml 2928 2932 2880 2884 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">poxB</italic>

###xml 2942 2946 2894 2898 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoS</italic>
###xml 2946 2947 2898 2899 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 2976 2980 2928 2932 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores2">[11]</xref>
###xml 2982 2986 2934 2938 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0007466-Flores5">[30]</xref>
